from today's Wall Street Journal(!)

Toad-Smoking Gains on Toad-Licking Among Drug Users

***

Toxic, Hallucinogenic Venom, Squeezed, Dried and Puffed, Has Others 
Turned Off

SAN FRANCISCO -- For the record, Mojo Nixon says neither he nor any 
members of his rock band, Mojo Nixon and the Toad Lickers, has ever 
actually licked a toad.

Still, with a name like that, Mr. Nixon's band can hardly help but 
attract attention from what authorities say is a small but growing 
segment of the drug culture that has taken up the bizarre practice of 
ingesting venom squeezed from live toads.  "People come up to us all 
the time and ask if we get high licking toads," says Mr. Nixon, who 
calls the very idea "insane."

Mojo knows.  He read something about toad-licking in the underground 
press about four years ago, and his band, the Burger Eaters, became 
the Toad Lickers.  Although tales of getting a buzz from lapping toad 
squeezings have circulated through underground lore since the 1960s, 
drug authorities on both sides of the law agree on one thing: Toad-
licking is not just weird but dangerous.

Warty Hoppers

Toad venom contains dozens of chemically active compounds, including 
enough poison to kill dogs that sometimes catch the warty little 
hoppers and try to eat them.  "I would think you could poison 
yourself pretty badly before you got high licking toads," says Andrew 
T. Well, an ethnopharmacologist at the University of Arizona's 
College of Medicine in Tuscon.

Thus, after a spurt of experimentation, toad-licking tapered off.

Toad-*smoking*, on the other hand, seems to be less risky and is on 
the rise, says Cecil Schwalbe, a research ecologist for the Interior 
Department.  Dr. Schwalbe says the heat from smoking venom appears to 
break down the toxins while retaining the psychedelics.  "The people 
who believe in better living through chemistry found out you could 
get the same hallucinogenic reaction from smoking toads as from 
licking them," he says.

Dr. Weil, a physician and drug-culture researcher, says that when he 
and a fellow researcher smoked dried venom from a Colorado River 
toad, it produced "a sense of wonder and well-being."

Dr. Weil's report, published two years ago in an obscure 
anthropological journal, Ancient Mesoamerica, apparently sent a smoke 
signal through the drug underground.

Arizona wildlife authorities recently raided the home of an 
unlicensed reptile-dealer near Tuscon and discovered dozens of 
football-sized Colorado-River toads sitting placidly in the man's 
living room.  (State law does allow possession of up to 10 toads if 
you have a fishing license.)  John Romero, law-enforcement program 
manager for the Arizona Department of Game and Fish, says his agents 
puzzled awhile over why anyone would have toads around the house.  
"Then the light came on," Mr. Romero says.

On the Southern California drug market these days, drug agents say a 
healthy toad can fetch up to $8.  One alleged dealer was arrested for 
illegal trading in wildlife last fall after he ran an ad in the 
University of Arizona student newspaper seeking a toad supply.

"Cane Toads." a 1989 documentary film that describes smoking toad 
venom in Australia, has become a cult-video favorite.  Toad-licking 
also came up recently on the television series "LA Law" (which 
mistakenly showed a bullfrog instead of a toad) and in an MTV "Beavis 
and Butt-head" cartoon.  "The show reflects what's going on in the 
youth culture," explains a "Beavis and Butt-head" spokeswoman.

Still, the whole toad thing is so bizarre that even critics are hard 
pressed to maintain a straight face.  South Carolina lawmakers 
giggled when a bill was introduced four years ago that would have 
made the state the first to outlaw toad-licking.  Rep. Patrick B. 
Harris, finding the practice "repulsive but amusing," proposed 
sentencing violators to 60 hours of public service in a local zoo.

Toads made the news again last month when California drug agents 
arrested Robert Shepard, a 41-year-old Boy Scout troop leader in 
Angels Camp, Calif., about 100 miles east of San Francisco.  Mr. 
Shepard was charged with several drug offenses, including possession 
of bufotenine, a chemical constituent of toad venom and a recognized 
hallucinogen.  The agents also impounded Mr. Shepard's four Colorado 
River toads -- Brian, Peter, Hans, and Franz.

Gregory Elam, the officer who made the arrest, says Mr. Shepard was 
so contrite he helped drug agents make a training video showing how 
venom is squeezed from kidney-shaped parotoid glands on the back of a 
live toad, then dried and smoked.  "It was pretty disgusting," says 
Mr. Elam, who has a big photograph of a toad on his office wall.  
"This is not something you would brag about to your mama."

Mr. Shepard won't talk to a reporter about toads or anything else.  
But James Webster, his attorney, says he himself had never heard of 
toad-smoking.  "I've heard of a princess kissing a toad," says Mr. 
Webster, misremembering the story of the frog prince.  "I guess these 
days she'd be busted, too."

Illegal Drug

Narcotics agents say Mr. Shepard may be the first person ever 
arrested on toad-smoking charges.  Bufotenine, as a hallucinogen, has 
been on federal and state dangerous-drug lists for years, and its 
possession is illegal.

In his Ancient Mesoamerica article, Dr. Weil reported that toad skins 
and artifacts depicting toads have turned up at Indian ceremonial 
sites in Mexico and Central America dating back more than a thousand 
years.  The researcher and others speculate that Mayans, Aztecs and 
other ancients may have used toad venom as an intoxicant in their 
rites.

Dr. Weil and his co-author, Wade Davis, theorize that the Colorado 
River toad has become the smokers' choice not because of bufotenine, 
but because it contains large amounts of the chemical compound 5-MeO-
DMT, a powerful psychoactive drug.

Experts describe the toad as a shy reptile found mostly in the 
Sonoran Desert in Northern Mexico and in the southern parts of 
Arizona and California.  The toads live underground most of the year, 
emerging only during the brief rainy season in midsummer.

The Colorado River toad, Dr. Weil says, is a virtual psychedelic 
factory, whose venom produces a 20-minute high that is so intense it 
can be frightening to the uninitiated.  "I've seen people take one 
deep puff and fall over backward as the exhale," he says.

'A Magical Slap'

Toad puffers, Dr. Weil says, usually are unresponsive for five 
minutes or more, making little noises until they open their eyes.  
Mr. Davis, a Washington anthropologist, calls the effect "a magical 
slap in the face."

That may be pleasing to toad-smokers, but it could mean problems for 
toads in the wild.  Dr. Weil says he has already received telephone 
calls from Californians eager to visit southern Arizona, where the 
critters are plentiful, to catch Colorado River toads.  "This looks 
like it could be a trend, and the toad is the one that will suffer," 
says Mr. Romero, the Arizona Game and Fish official worried about 
depleting the toad population.

The toad's protector, say officials, will probably be environmental 
laws, not drug laws.  California, for example, began implementing a 
law last week that makes it a misdemeanor to possess any of the 
shrinking population of Colorado River toads in the state.

"Eventually," says Mr. Elam, the Angels Camp drug agent, "you'll 
probably see a much stiffer penalty for possession of a toad than for 
a controlled substance.  The environmentalists have more clout than 
the cops."

------- End of Forwarded Message

This seems like a popular heading lately, but I'm writing a paper on
raves, and I need to know how people view rave music and rave culture. 
Where did it come from?  Where is it going?  Could it be related to the
sort of mocking of commercialism found in pop art?  Is techno the next in
a long line of deviations from a norm, or is it the norm itself,
simplified almost beyond recognition?

Any ideas?  Write me..

marinmarin

Subject: Greening*Newbie*FMR*Badges
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Interesting, all this talk of "newbies," Greening of America,"  and "Badges."
Being someone who is a 9 month newbie to Sfraves, having read "Greening" when
it was first published (and still have my copy), and going through what many
of you are talking about as it pertains to the Rave community. It has been 
slightly more difficult  for me  to  begin coming to the raves. I was your
classic 42 year-old, lost-love-generation academic, divorced, mid-life
melt-down kinda guy.  A friend of a friend, introduced me to a 49 year old
Doctor who prescribed two-pills, dance all night at a rave, and call him in
the morning. "Sweet mystery of life at last I've found you," or at least
found you again! I want you all to know I've gotten every conceivable
reaction at the raves.  For example, "I'm not gonna give you a flyer cause
you look like a narc," "What are YOU doing here?" to  "I wish my dad was
here!" "I've seen you at other parties and I wanted to come up and say
hello!"--Garth, and Rick Preston always make a point to say Hi!-because they
know I drive up and back from Monterey each weekend, and that I love this
music. My friend, Forrest and I have taken to calling ourselves the "Monterey
Rave Posse." We are  happy when the FMR's come to BD beach, cause it's only
40 minutes away to home. This last rain-soaked FMR was particularly blissful.
I'll probably put SFraves-MRP on my badge. Come up and say hello. The
"Consciousness III" chapter from THE GREENING OF AMERICA, meant a lot to me.
Why the movement died before  is because we automatically excluded people who
were, different, older,  and not "in." I suggest that if you think your scene
will always be here, I offer this warning: That if you don't include, and
nourish others, and bring them in with love and kindness, the music will die.
 We blamed it all on the establishment until we became it, and "filthy Lucre"
$$$$$$ taught us not to care so much. And we finally gave up who we were. I
did for about ten years. At the raves I've remembered what it was like to
care, to believe, to free up my soul through dance, and stand in awe of the
music coming out of those big black square boxes. Magic boxes, with magicians
juggling spinning black wheels in front of them. All this has charmed my
soul, and it keeps my feet dancing, and my toes tapping.(during the week
also) For someone who began with underground radio in the 60"s, the Grammy
Awards" were a sad commentary on what happens when money gets its hands at
the throat of Artists and Musicians. We should be thankful there isn't a
catagory called, "Best New Rave Single." Remember to Remember--"To Rave is to
Affirm." See ya at the parties--Robert (MRP)

I found this amusing anecdote on rec.music.gdead when I was doing research 
for Atomic Dog and have been since looking for an excuse to repost it:
----------------------------------------------------------------------
I am absolutely not making this incident up; 
in fact I have it all on videotape.  The tape is 
from a local TV news show in Oregon, which 
sent a reporter out to cover the removal of a 
45-foot, eight-ton dead whale that washed up 
on the beach.  The responsibility for getting rid 
of the carcass was placed with the Oregon 
State Highway Division, apparently on the 
theory that highways and whales are very 
similar in the sense that both are large objects.
So anyway, the highway engineers hit upon a 
plan (remember, I am not making this up) to 
blow up the whale with dynamite. The thinking 
was that the whale would be blown into small 
pieces, which would then be eaten by seagulls 
and fish.  That would be that, a textbook whale 
removal.  So they moved the spectators back up 
the beach, put a half-ton of dynamite next to 
the whale and set it off.  What follows, on the 
videotape, is one the most priceless events in 
the history of the universe.  First you see the 
whale carcass disappear in a huge blast of 
smoke and flame.  Then you hear the happy 
spectators shouting "Yayy!" and "Whee!" Then, 
suddenly, the crowd's tone changes. You hear 
a new sound like "splud, splap", and you hear 
a woman's voice shouting "Here come pieces 
of...OH MY GOD!"  Something smears the camera 
lens.  Later, the reporter explains: "The humor 
of the entire situation suddenly gave way to a 
run for survival as huge chunks of whale blubber 
rained down everywhere."  One piece caved in 
the roof of a car parked more than a quarter 
of a mile away!!  Remaining on the beach were 
several large rotting whale sections the size 
of condominiums.  There was no sign of the 
seagulls who had no doubt had permanently 
relocated to Brazil.
-------------------------------------------------------------
ObRave: Some of the best parties happen on beaches.

Yep.  I live in Oregon.  I lived here then.  It really happened; I've
seen the video on the news.  

The Highway Department (actually the Department of Transportation) is
responsible for beaches, because in Oregon (motto: Things look
different here) all beaches are considered state highways, even though
motorized vehicles are banned on most beaches most of the time.

This was a bizzare consequence of actions by a Governor over fifty
years ago, and was done to preserve public access to beaches.

So the whale was their problem.  It was different opening the paper to
headlines like "Transportation Department to Dispose of Rotting Whale
with Dynamite" and "Giant Chunks of Whale Still Rotting on Beach."  I
can't remember the exact words, but something like that.

Oh, and in case anyone cares, I've been to the mall where Tonya
Harding practices, it's right accross the freeway from the "New Hope
Community Church," effectively a religion mall.  The combined
facilities offer one-stop shopping for all your secular and spiritual
needs.  I've never voted for Bob Packwood.  I met Ken Kesey one time
in Eugene, he was nice but in kind of a hurry.

- Erik

	Amusing note to stories of whale demolition:

	When I was about 15, I wanted to be a marine biologist.  I lived 
in Portland at the time, and got hooked up with one of the professors at 
Portland State who studied whales.  One of her fields of interest was 
beached whales.  The deal she had worked out was that she got to hear 
about and study any whale, as long as her crew disposed of it.  Most of 
the whales were 20-30 feet long, and small charges and shovels usually 
did the trick (plus warning the locals that great white sharks would come 
from miles around).  Interesting hobby for any young boy :)

	Usually, we'd plant charges just big enough to break the thing 
up, and drag the pieces into the surf.  I'll spare you all the details.  
The point of all this was, I got a call to come out to the coast one 
day.  There was a huge whale, and the Highway Division (I believe this is 
because Oregon beaches are technically public thoroughfares.  Stops 
developing.) wanted our advice on how to get rid of the thing before 
tourist weekend.

	So we told them to use explosives.  Never thought they'd use that 
much.  Believe me, they put enough TNT into that thing to blow up the 
Sears Tower.  I have never seen something so, well, gory, in my life as 
500-pound chunks of whale attempting to reach escape velocity.

	Needless to say, that was the end of the Cetacean Detonation 
Project.  Quite soon after, I found a more useful and healthy hobby.

	ObRave: None.  Just thought I'd confirm today's wierdness.

	Jesse

        ("the CA hemp initiative will legalize marijuana for

        (415) 281-KNOW

        3-7pm free at ameba to celebrate the
        completion of our media-poor media and tea lounge. (1732 Haight)

        In the 'Pepper Room' DJ Digit & EFX, Rasoul, Chris Lum, Markie Mark,
        Noel, and Buck. And in the 'Jazid Up' Room: Ammon, Mark
        Farina, and probably Thomas.
        everyone is invited (even if you don't know buck or sara).
        Sound Factory, 525 Harrison, SF. 9-4AM.

        415.905.5700  510.287.9392

        Josh  Spun  Simon  Graeme  DJ Dan  Jeno
        415.266.8215

        a gala cosmopolitan affair benefitting Big Brothers/Big Sisters
        DJs jellybear, henrik, suiki, rick preston, rebecca
        1015 Folsom.  Info: 415.386.8749

Saturday, March 26th - Ambience

        Namlook (Frankfurt) plus

Subject: Bowling Fraud
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Message-Id: <Pine.3.89.9403110015.D15645-0100000@uclink.berkeley.edu>
Mime-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; charset=US-ASCII

I've just returned from a not so short round trip from Berkeley to SF and 
back.  Why am I back so soon, you ask?  Well, after seeing the Spun@Rock'n Bowl
event mentioned several times on the list (including on the calendar), I 
thought it would be fun to go bowling (which we were thinking about doing 
anyway) and to see Spun play for just 5 bucks, bowling fees included.  I 
called up the bowling alley and all seemed dandy.  We arrived, entered, 
made our way up to the cash register, and THEN... it happened:

"That'll be five dollars, and I'll need to see your ID's", said the bitch.

"What??!!!??" (very surprised)

"Come back when you're 21."

First of all, this statement alone pissed me off.  Where do door people 
get off saying derogatory shit like that?  She didn't look 21 herself.  

Second, not ONCE was it ever mentioned on this list (or anywhere else 
for that matter),that you had to be 21 years old to go bowling in San 
Francisco.  I even remember past Rock 'n Bowl/rave events mentioned, 
never with the 21+ stipulation.  I can't blame Derek, because I'm sure he 
didn't know, but didn't SOMEONE know?  Things like this shouldn't go 
unmentioned.  Needless to say, I think the whole thing is pretty fucked (even 
21+ clubs in general).  I know this thread has been dealt with many times 
before, but the fact is, the only reason for having a 21+ event is 
$$$$$$.  It costs more money to obtain the permits for 18+, so heck, if 
we can discriminate against younger people AND save money, then why the 
hell not?  Enough said.

Seth

Well, the problem was with the NIN unannounced show at the Temple was it 
was NEVER announced (at least I never heard them mention) that it was a 
21+ place.  I was major bummed.  There was also an unannounced show at 
The Edge friday for $5.  That WOULD have been cool, but I actually like 
other bands way more.  I need to save my cash anyway.  

On the Bowling thing.  When I called (XXX-BOWL), i got some dude who just 
said "hello?"  I got confused and thought I had a wrong #.  Still, that 
was completely overshadowed by the lack-of-attention-to-detail of LIVE 
105 to not mention the fact that you HAD to be 21+ (or have a fake ID).  
I think shit like this encourages us discriminated youths to REBEL and go 
out and get one!  I mean, we get our hopes up only to be broken up at the 
door.  I didn't even see ANY signs saying this while we waited about 15 
minutes in line.  I know of one way to get a fake one, but that way takes 
like 2 months! (it's the phoney birth cert/SS#- send it to Sac. way...) 
Is there any quicker way (besides using a GOOD scanner/digitizer)???
Oh well, just my 2cents.

I'm normally not a fan of indoor raves - they're too loud (can't hide from
   the sound, which I want to do at least per night for an hour maybe), you
   can't "take a walk", they're usually in especially seedy neighborhoods
   (read: safe to park?), they're often expensive, and ...

Kindness was none^H^H^H^Hfew of these things.  First: the music was
   intense... the big names did their shit.  The vibe was there...

The space was pretty neat, although it could have had more... stuff...
   filling it up - more sofas in some places... nothing hanging frmo the
   walls really, and overall kinda hasty... but the visuals in the main
   dance floor were perfect.

The organizers were -very- cool.  I had to run back to the car for a minute
   and they were cool with it... they didn't especially try to rip you off
   on liquids... the t-shirts for sale were most.

anyway, time to faceplant.

dreams be merry,
adam

Now, *THIS* was a good event!  $7.00 at the door, bumpin' sound, and a good
cause!  This party was all about the heart of "rave".  Reminded me of my
old LA days in '91-'92.  Lots of people (all ages), having a good time.

Even though I generally do not attend 21-- events, this one was worth
checking out at least.  It is one of the *very few* places 21--- can go and
stay ALL NIGHT.  I was dismayed that the place was not packed out by the
time I left (1:30), becuase it should have been.
Nice one from the MESS crew (this was the *FIRST* MESS event I've
attended)!  And a big thanks to Brad for inviting me!  Hopefully I'll be
able to stay longer next time.  It was also nice to see some of the SFR
posse there (Bryce, Ethan, Moni, Tom, & Larry)!

Pet peeves:
That fucking party should have been overflowing!  But due to *many* people
bad mouthing the *VENUE* for such long periods of time, it will be
difficult for anyone to have an event decently attended.  I know there has
been some shitty events that have happened at the Haze, but that is *NOT*
the venues fault.  Instead it is the fault of the promoters/priducers of
the party.  Instead of attacking the individuals, a concerted effort was
made to di the space.  Now people with perfectly good intentions, who may
choose the space, have a difficult time overcoming the rep the place has
developed.  This is both stupid, *and* unfortunate for the scene.  That
place  could bring in many many new people.  It has *many* advantages, like
being *all ages*, all night!  Oh well, I've talked this game before...good
luck to anybody throwing an event there.  Alot of damage thru word of mouth
has been done.  Only time will turn things around for the HAZE. BTW I found
the security there FINE!  Not oppressive, and they really weren't walking
around bothering folx.  Now that's good security.

Another peeve is smoke.  I do not smoke cigs, never have, never will.  I
*hate* the smell of over processed tobacco, it fucking stinks!  Of all the
drugs it is the *MOST* oppressive.   Pot is another matter, the stuff
smells funkiddidly sweet.  Some would say it stinks as well, but the thing
is, pot smoke don't stick around.  You can air it out, it is natural, and
is not produced by Phllip Morris (yet).  Cigs do not have any of these
characteristics.  There was no booze at the Haze, but PLENTY of young
junkies (cigarette that is) for Phillip Morris.  Sad.  I just hate the
smell of the stuff and wish there was just a bit more ventillation.  I was
there for 1.5 hours, and by the time I got home I smelled like club funk.
Arrgh!!!  I think my next club will be called IONIZER, whose motto will be
"Getting the FUNK out yo face!".  I hate cigs....

Old boyz network:
Here we are, the start of '94.  Shit is heating up and I'ma
wondering...where are all the ladies?  You know, of the DJ variety?  Where
are those tapes ladies?  How come I can go into Ameba, Tribal, BPM, and see
many of the boyz (i.e. any male dj archetype) tapes, while I see zero from
the better sex?  I hope that YSH is *NOT* the only place you can hear
ladies go off on the decks.  I hope that in '94 the ladies make a big push
to get some exposure from other sides of the scene.  Only thru diversity
can things grow.  And *I* am always interested in getting new people who
have the touch, and can do the do.

Good Housekeeping will always be looking for people for our Guest Spots, as
well as many other clubs.  Nuff said....

On that Good Housekeeping tip:
We raised the door price 1 buck to $4.00.
There will be many offerings for breakfast, from $1-$3 bucks:a nice gourmet
breakfast will do wonders.  The $3 range will feature more feature filled
dishes.  But you WILL eat quite well for $1-$2.  There will be a MENU to
choose from. So...get your feet, stomach, and *MIND* ready for Good
Housekeeping on the 20th.

Harry Who will be there doin the do in the back with James, Alfie, and
Markie, along with Disco Detective Sassy Lime, getting soulful and funky in
the front.  Live Jazz will also be featured.

Ok, my shameless promotion is up, and so is this message.


Pax,
John

16th & Harrison deserves its bad reputation for a long string of
overhyped, overpriced parties with obnoxious security, second-rate
sound and a vibe that would make fresh paint peel.  

I've been to a few things there over a couple of years and only went
to one that was any good -- an unannounced free thing on a Sunday
evening about six months ago.

Let's face it, the place is an anti-power spot for our scene.  Not
to say that it can't be used, and I'm glad MESS made good use of it.
If I'd been in town I would probably have gone.  But it's not clear,
as jslee intimates, that club nights are totally separable from the
spaces they are held in.  The management attitude at 16th & Harrison
pervades the place just as that at Townsend or 1015 or DV8 or any place
else does.  

As for women DJs, last time I was at BPM -- last Tuesday, actually, there
were not one, not two, but THREE different DRC tapes available (including
her new one 'Ritual Addiction' which she described to me as being 'mellow' :)

There are plenty of male DJs who get regular gigs in SF who do not put
tapes out in general circulation.  I've never seen a Hardkiss (any variety)
tape, for example.  That's not to say they're not out there, but I am an
avid tape collector and I know what's out there.

As an aspiring DJ of sorts myself, I know something about the barriers
women DJs face in getting gigs.  You have to have a rep to get gigs,
and you have to have gigs to get a rep.  It's a slow process, and the
historical fact is that women in music as in many fields don't get
full consideration of their talents.  Breaks are a matter of hard work
*and* support from the scene.  That's why it's so important for things
like YSH to happen which provide some visibility for some DJs who
otherwise would remain mostly out of public view.

*PROVE* that something good can happen at that space.  And the vibe was a
nice one this past Saturday.  I just wanna know.  Where in SF do 21-- go?
Nuff said.  Everything, and everyone deserves a second chance, and if what
Kindness did was  any example, everyone should be up for at least
reconsidering their stance on Haze.

>

I do not agree.  The ONLY thing that is anti-power is attitudes, pissy
cops, and  shitty promoters (some of which RAN that space for a while).
Just call em crazy, I do not believe in bad buildings as a rule.

>Not

That's only because people wanna make that quick non-thinking connection.
The FACT is a promoter rents a space to use.  If I don't like the promoter
or what he/she stands for I do not attend their events.  If I would apply
your logic to the situation, I would have stayed home and not even given
the boys from MESS a chance.  This is just not fair, to judge a
promoter/posse/team by the space they use.  And that's what you end up
doing.  Whatever...just another reason the scene suffered last year.  This
year though, I hope others throw things there so that it's rep can get
built up again.  And it is also a cool place for 21--.  The ONLY one in SF!

Not true.  It was all Kindnesstude at that place!  ANYTHING can be overcome

>
>As for women DJs, last time I was at BPM -- last Tuesday, actually, there
>were not one, not two, but THREE different DRC tapes available (including
>her new one 'Ritual Addiction' which she described to me as being 'mellow' :)

I have heard of DRC.  I stand corrected for the statment of seeing ZERO
from a female DJ (Noting Laura's previous correction).  However, one tape
ain't enough.  And it is REALLY not a tape issue, but an issue of getting
to hear female DJ's out and about, *NOT* just at one party.  It's all about
getting out there, not hunkering down.  I still wanna hear MORE from the
ladies of this scene (i.e. DJ's).

>
>There are plenty of male DJs who get regular gigs in SF who do not put
>tapes out in general circulation.

Like who?  Before you answer that, the male dj's who get regular gigs
*HAVE* put out tapes aplenty before.  Secondly, their rep is secure and
they play a variety of places, so they are always out there.  And last,
promoters exchange tapes, and I consider that circulation.  That is where
recommendations come in, and that's the point.  There are a couple of guys
I know who are really good but have not gotten the bookings, they are
getting the word out there about their abilities, and as a result are
gettin play.  The same effort should (and is by some) be made by the
greatly unheard from female DJ's.  It's happening, but on a smaller scale
and slowly.  I just wish it would happen on a lrger scale and quickly.

>I've never seen a Hardkiss (any variety)
>tape, for example.  That's not to say they're not out there, but I am an
>avid tape collector and I know what's out there.

I have several HK tapes.  And they are all over the place as most DJ tapes
are.  Seeing it in stores is just one idicator.  Albeit a good indication
of who's doing what (when was the last time you heard HK spin?).

>
>As an aspiring DJ of sorts myself, I know something about the barriers
>women DJs face in getting gigs.  You have to have a rep to get gigs,

>historical fact is that women in music as in many fields don't get
>full consideration of their talents.  Breaks are a matter of hard work
>*and* support from the scene.  That's why it's so important for things
>like YSH to happen which provide some visibility for some DJs who
>otherwise would remain mostly out of public view.

YSH is fine, but relying on *one* party alone for exposure may not be the
best course for some.  I just think that people should branch out, and do a
variety of gigs.  Now I have never attended a YSH, but will do so this year
when it gets started.

There is no reason for fusion NOT to happen in SF this year. This place
should go ballistic with the number of DJ's kinda stable, and people
wanting something new.  The time is now for newer DJ's to get in while they
are still able to.  It's all about making that connection, communicating,
saying hello (for the most part), and passin' that tape.

Audi from all this.  We'll see what becomes of '94,
John

ELECTRONIC EAVESDROPPING
A measure soon to be introduced on Capitol Hill would require that all
network providers, including the Internet and commercial on-line services,
build in the capability to record any person's e-mail and deliver it to
federal law-enforcement authorities. Government agents will need only to

Hello - Larry Ching here ...

In reaction to the recent "Kindness" posts , Fred Heutte replied:
> From: "Fred Heutte" <phred@well.sf.ca.us>
> 
> 16th & Harrison deserves its bad reputation for a long string of
> overhyped, overpriced parties with obnoxious security, second-rate
> sound and a vibe that would make fresh paint peel.  
> 
> Let's face it, the place is an anti-power spot for our scene.  Not
> to say that it can't be used, and I'm glad MESS made good use of it.
> If I'd been in town I would probably have gone.i
>
 Too bad you couldn't make it , you would have definitly enjoyed it!
I had a great time ; hit some nice trancey mind spaces about three times
that night.

 I had an omen that things were going to turn out OK when I showed up
at the door at 11:30PM to find one of the SFRavers at the door! I 
don't quite remember her name ( Diane? I warned you I'm lousy with names!
Nice to have met your SO ). And , once inside , there was Lavonne (?)
and another guy named Sun , sitting on the sofa behind the ticket
taker.

 I managed to meet a bunch of folks from SFRaves - the Normals, Fogels
( pssst! Lee , what was your wife's name again ??? [ I was there was 
a drug to improve name memory ...] ), John G/"Jump In The Fire", Marlo ,
Bryce , Ethan , Larry(?) , John Draper. As far as the crowd was concerned ,
seem to be the usual rave club party mix , except with a somewhat younger 
crowd than a club , more like an FMR. Some packs of guys trying too
look tough , but they seem to be more concerned with projecting that
image instead of proving it, so things were OK there.

 Some mentioned that more furniture would have been nice - I thought 
they proved more comfy chairs and cushions than a lot of other $15++
spaces. There was a nice spot behind the big stage that had a few
chairs , that I curled up in for a shoort nap.

 As in other events , the "chill room" DJ seemed to be a tad deaf - I
didn't think he had to compete for the sound as much as he did. Sound iso
isolation of the chill space from the other dance areas was much better
than Richmond Civic. The chill area was smaller than Richmond's , and
the flow of traffic is right through the middle ( the room was actually
a wide hallway ).

 The Haze Theatre itself was on "its" best behaviour. Not too obnoxious
security ( only one bust that I've heard of , and I don't even know if
the guy in question was kicked out or not - caught lighting up the herb
of the event ). Sound in both rooms was quite adequate , not distorted
to any harsh/earshreadding degree . Crowd vibe - mellow enough! 

----------------------------

 KINDNESS was a great event! I wish more folks had shown up , for the
MESS / benefit's sake. 

----------------------------

 So - which Promoters/Events have been held at the Haze Theatre that
were real stinkers? 

----------------------------

	Larry Ching/larryc@netcom.com

PS - John G. , how did you get home?

I'm really glad the event took off. I helped a bit with setup and
provided a little of the deco, and all of the promoters were just
totally nice people. I crashed out at a friends house and headed over
after 3am (still sleep deprived mind you) at which point things were
beginning to wind down a bit.

If you haven't heard Brad or Scottie spin, check them out. I really
enjoyed their sets.

The Haze theatre *is* a creepy place. It takes a lot of visuals and
positive energy to overcome it, but it can be done. The security was
pretty cool actually outdoors. Indoors, however, they were too
aggressive about looking for drugs. (Why do they bother?) It's
vibe-upsetting to see cops craning their necks every time someone
hands something to someone else. I'm strongly tempted to go around
"dealing" chewing gum some night just to frustrate the police.

Except for that, I thought things were pretty good. And the price was
right, too. 

Sean

From: csc@pilot.njin.net (Sean Casey)
Message-Id: <9403141904.AA23315@pilot.njin.net>
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: New Moon Rave review 3/11
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Wow. This event was the perfect renegade. It was held somewhere (not
telling) on a beach in Point Reyes. The weather was perfect: a cool
but not cold night, and a light offshore (dry) breeze.

There were about 30 people there, enough to make it a party, but few
enough that I learned a lot of names and made some new friends :). The
Hardkisses (and a couple of DJs whose names I didn't catch) provided
some good sets. The music was a bit ambient and experimental at
times, at others flowing into a deep house or trance set. 

This party just had phenomenal good vibes. Mona and many of the others
(Hi anthrax!)  at the party are some of the nicest people I've
met in the scene in a while. I've been going to too many parties with
too much ego, and this one just felt like a big cozy hug.

At one time I walked off for a while, and turned around, and it was
so neat seeing the people around the fire in the distance, with the
stars so bright and so close overhead. A moonless night has its own
special charms :).

I strongly recommend checking out this free party, especially if huge
event nitrous/booze/ego/whatever has got you down. Very good for the
soul.

Sean

Subject:  RE: Kindness and Haze Theater

Just a few comments about Kindness and the Haze Theater:


I really enjoyed the event even though it was at the Haze Theater.
My friends and I have been to several events at the Haze Theater in
the past, and had such negative experiences that we vowed never to
go again.  The only reason that we went to Kindness was that we are
friends with Brad (one of the MESS djs) and wanted to support his
event.  Also, with only $7.00 for a cover charge, we felt that we
weren't risking too much to attend.  Unfortunately, many of our
friends did not show up because it was at the Haze Theater.

When I mentioned this to Brad at the party, he said that he knew
that the Haze Theater had a bad reputation, but that it was the only
place that they could find in SF that would allow under 21 all
night.  He did mention that the ONLY problems they had in putting on
the event were trying to deal with the management at the Haze
Theater...

In summary, the event was great - music, visuals, everything.  The
only drawback was that there should have been many more people in
attendance.  I hope that MESS events are able to draw more people in
the future - they're a great bunch of people and deserve to be
supported.


- Chris

just my random observations of sat's kindness party:

expected the worst after finding out it was at Haze...
but was pleasantly surprised by a good party with great music and
friendly people inside.  i concure with jsl on the smoke thing...after
dancing for awhile, the last thing you want is to take a big breath of
stinky cig. smoke - burning budz are like incense to me though.

i wandered from the main room to the back mess rooms almost exclusively.  it
was a toss up which was better.  both were great for different reasons.  the 
mess room i though was trippyer and i could take my ear plugs
out and get bugged in the brain.  the main floor was high energy body music.
i love dancing right in front of the stacks - feels good.

only ventured upstairs to the ambient room twice.  i liked the info tables on
mj and the table with the psychoactive plant samples.  picked up all info
that was available.  good info.

all and all a good time worht the price and cause...

a shout out to 'mike' for reading my mind - thx for the 'shrooms!

barry

Hi folks!

First of all, let me say on behalf of the Mother Earth Sound System: 
Thank you, to all those that volunteered at, promoted for, attended or 
otherwise supported KINDNESS - your help was greatly appreciated!!!  
Although various aspects of putting on the party disturbed us, we all 
agreed that for our first effort at an indoor event, we shouldn't 
complain too much :)  More importantly, we broke even, and got over 400 
(whoopee!) signatures for the California Hemp Initiative, which was the 
primary reason for doing KINDNESS in the first place.  BTW, if anyone is 
curious about our budget and expenses for this party, just email me 
directly and I'll pass the info your way.

Regarding the discussion that's been going on about the Haze Theatre, its
owners, etc, I have to admit that we came away from this party with a
pretty bad taste in our mouths, but now that its all over, we're just glad
the party went as well as it did.  Like many of you, I believe that the
bad rep that the Haze Theatre has been saddled with may be due largely to
past promoters and the sort of events they have thrown there, but I'm not
hesitant to say that the current owners are to be blamed for a lot of the
negative energy that is associated with the space.  Why?  Well, just based
on our experience with them, they're profit-hungry, which automatically
(at least the way I see it) prevents them from doing right by the 
promoters and party-goers that they cater to.  Specific examples?  I 
don't want to start listing all our grievances with them, but suffice it 
to say that if you're trying to throw a 18+ event in the city, please try 
to find an alternative to the Haze Theatre (at least while it's under the 
current management), for your own good (financially and 
mentally/emotionally) and the interests of your partygoers.  We learned 
the hard way, and were fortunate that the good vibes that you and many 
others poured into the party made it go off.

Fortunately, it seems not too many of you had bad experiences with the 
security, but I have heard of at least 4 instances of confiscated pot 
-- two of my friends got their pipes taken, and NOT returned :(  This all 
happened despite us repeatedly telling them to lay off.  I'm also glad 
there were no serious problems with obtaining water, but since Jimmy 
(owner) was selling it and juice (something we found out Sat. afternoon), 
he prevented us from giving out free water and OJ as we had planned.

Sorry to go on about stuff that a lot of you have already discussed, but 
I just wanted to let you all know where the Mother Earth Sound System 
stands regarding that space and its owners.  And BTW, you might be seeing 
some "guest posts" from my address, from some other MESS members who have 
stuff to say about the party.

Thanks once again for the support you've given us -- many of you, at some 
point, in various ways, have reminded us of why we are doing what we're 
doing, and we love you for helping us create the community and parties 
that we all want to have :).  With that in mind, we hope to see you all at 
our first outdoor party of the year, our 1 year anniversary, on 
Saturday, April 2 (NOT April 3 as we mistakenly said before).  Fun in the 
springtime sun!!!

Peace & respect,

			*************************
			s   c   o   t   t   i   e
			*************************
			MOTHER EARTH SOUND SYSTEM
			*************************
			>>>respect your mother<<<
			*************************

You're right!  I didn't even think of that!  The Ethan that I 
referenced is a local DJ who spins PHAT house, sweet dub-stylee and 
alpha-wave ambient.  And whoay did he deeeeeliver...in fact, everyone 
there spun some great vinyl.

Union & Transcendance was held at the Sailor's Pacific Union Hall, 2505 
1st Avenue in Seattle.  The building managment was really cool; in fact 
at the end of the night they invited us back.   That's some pretty good 
news given the scarcity of decent spaces in Seattle; often building 
managment doesn't want anything to do with the house community after 
their space has been trashed and abused by give-a-shit prometers who 
see a one-off as a way to make quick bucks, leaving a huge trail of 
debris.  I really wish that promoters would put energy in cultivating 
the relationship between the house community and property owners; 
leaving a space as good or better than The turnout was okay, nothing 
stellar.  I would guess that about 300-325 people were in attendance 
over the course of the night (the hall itself has a capacity of 350) 
with about 200 people at any one time.  From what I hear, many people 
decided not to go because they felt there would be a "weird vibe" or 
something.  On the other hand, I hear (second hand from people who 
_didn't_ go to the party) that those who came thought it to be a phat 
party, which was the whole point of the event.  The proceeds are on 
their way to the family.  Thanks again, everyone who came, contributed 
and just had fun.  And thanks to all of you who sent your best wishes.  
Riz spun funky old house, Masa left wax prints on our brains, Hebegebe, 
Quest and Donald worked us over with a mixture of hardbeats and Dervish 
closed the set with a mixture of trance, house and ambient that left us 
all in awe of the masterful bridging and his beautiful choice of last 
song which went well with our gathering hand-in-hand in a big circle to 
celebrate coming back together.

Rhthm&Bass

Peace!

	>>Greg

> A measure soon to be introduced on Capitol Hill would require that all
> network providers, including the Internet and commercial on-line services,
> build in the capability to record any person's e-mail and deliver it to
> federal law-enforcement authorities.

This sounds like the "FBI Wiretap Proposal."  It is being introduced
for the second (or third?) time.  The resurfacing of this proposal, at
this time, is unlikely to be coincidental, but has a lot to do with
the Clipper/Skipjack/Capstone proposal.  Combine a guarantee of access
to all communication with a guarantee to be able to decrypt all
communication, and routine automated domestic spying becomes feasible
and cost-effective.

Some parts of the US Government appear to be very serious about not
allowing civil society to exist in cyberspace, and by extention
anywhere. 

- Erik

Erik Nilsson, CPSR (Computer Professionals for Social Responsibility)

>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>
Speaking of Hardkisses;  Did they ever get their equipment back from
the rip-off in Salt Lake City.  I usually don't hear about outcomes!
<<<<<<<<<<<<<<<

	The Hardkisses didn't lose any equipment, but they did get ripped
off their wages.  The unfortunate people that lost equipment were
sound and light rental people here in Salt Lake.  I hear the FBI has
a file on Davey (the sleazy promoter that caused all this shit) and
is now hunting him down.  Hopefully they will bust his ass, because
he's caused quite a lot of damage to the great but smaller scene we
have here.  Now it's impossible for a promoter to rent sound without
also paying the rental people to watch it all night long, just so
they can insure that it won't "walk off" like Davey's system did.
	If anybody ever does meet a shady guy with a Uhaul truck full of
light and sound from out of state...  Well, you know what to do.  And
also please keep in mind that Davey's actions in no way speak for the
rest of Salt Lake.  We've tried to do nothing more than build a great
vibe here and we've had some great parties.  I know personally that
these promoters have never ripped anyone off:  Mechanized, Playscool,
Taste, Phunk Productions, and Guru.

Peace, Love, and Bass...

Luke

Rick Preston and Jeno in San Jose!!! I thought. I called my friend  Forrest
and we agreed to "damn to torpedoes" and leave Monterey at 9:30 and expect to
get home by 3:00am.  WE'd find a way to drag our reluctant bodies to work the
next day.  First, Rick met us at the door and informed us Julius would our DJ
before Jeno, and that he would be playing NEXT Wed. OK, Julius played a
competent housey set, but there realy wan't a crowd vibe yet. Jeno went on at
12:00 and elevated the music, the house, and the crowd. The guy's atomic!
The last two times I saw him; Spundae and Wicked were orbital, and last night
was no different. Just when you think you've crested in a groove, he presses
the time-warp button, and yanks everyone up a notch! If you haven't been to
MOTION at the FX, it's a little funny. The club is burrowed in behind a movie
theater in downtown SJ. The dance floor is graduated where movie seats used
to be, so you're at a slight incline. It's like dancing at the Santa Cruz
Mystery Spot!!! WE left at 1:40, and got home at 2:50am.(maintaining the
speed limit all the way) Had a grreat time; remember Rick is playing next
Wed. Robertj..Monterey Rave Posse.

Oops, I almost forgot to send this today.  I might be missing some
stuff because I haven't been out lately, so I dunno what's up on 
Friday.  On Saturday, Equinox returns after what seems like a long
hiatus (or else they've been way underground).  I remember a great
Equinox back in spring '92, but then they were a bit inconsistent
after that.  Organic also returns Saturday, it'll be big, it'll
probably be $20, but if you go in expecting that, you can have fun.
If you can stay up, or if you skip all that, check out the opening
of Good Housekeeping on Sunday morning...

I won't comment on the Orb video as I haven't seen it. I have however=
 seen the toon town, full moon, etc. video. While it's a nice "document"=
 of the happenings it's also your average "humanoid with a handicam"=
 special, which, IMO, isn't worth $20 let alone $50. If I'm gonna=
 spend *money* I'd like some *production values* like a direct audio=
 feed from the mixer (as opposed to camcorder miking), full sets=
 instead of half of a song from this dj, a scrap of that song from=
 that dj, etc.

Make no mistake, I'm glad someone's out there getting this stuff,=
 I just think their prices need to re-enter this solar system.

take it easy
ethan

Some of you have requested info on the C.H.I., so here's all the dope ;) 
on it that I could round up:

CHI Hotline: 1 (800) 425-HEMP

Deadline for petitions: May 27

Total # sigs needed: 500,000
  (actually only 380,000, but they have to allow for procedural error)

Want to volunteer?  Easy 30 min. petitioner training sessions every Sat 
and Sun betw. 10 am and noon at the Hemporium, 442A Haight (near 
Fillmore).

You can sign the petition at the Hemporium, open Tu-Sun 11-5, or call 
them and ask for a place in your area, (415) 552-7487.

We should realize the potential we have as a community to support this
cause, and act accordingly.  Just look at KINDNESS as an example: out of
about 650-700 people that attended, over _500_ signed the CHI, and over
100 registered to vote.  That's over _two-thirds_ folks!!!  Just imagine
the results you could get if you and your friends took petitions with you
when you went to parties, to clubs, to the park, etc etc!  At KINDNESS, we
had great success by petitioning to the people standing in line, and
putting a table with info and hemp products up in the chill room.  C'mon,
let's unite and legalize marijuana in this state!!! 

Peace + respect,
scottie

Jeez, i knew i shoulda uns!bbed from the list when I was gone. Netcom 
left me a nice note saying my mailbox had grown past the preset limit and 
did a little compression job on my incoming messages.

As I was (finally) getting off the plane to D'troit, I turned around to 
see...Shoban! Apparently she's going to be out there with Chris for a 
while. They've got a big loft downtown (prob for half the price o'mine) 
and Chris is going to have a release out on Switch soon.

On the way back I had a layover in St.Louis where (I swear) they've got 
those metal detectors jacked up high enough to beep if you've got too 
much iron in your blood. I must have matched some hijacker profile or 
something. Beep. Take off coat. Beep. Remove change and keys. Beep. 
lighter. Beep. Took off necklace. Beep. Belt (after all, I could've 
gutted a crewmember in under five seconds with the buckle or something). 
Beep. Boots. Beep. Unload 9mm pistol stashed in hollow leg. Beep. Remove 
skull plate. Beep. take out tooth fillings... beep

Little did they know, I watch MacGyver too, and with a little effort I 
was able to contruct a crude low-yield nuclear explosive from my belt 
buckle, the in-flight magazine, 2 straws, a spork, 130 g ice, and a stick 
of gum. I was then able to hold my neighbor hostage until I was given 
another bag of honey-roasted peanuts. Ah, sweet sucrose, all thanks to 
the moons gravitational pull and the density of oxygen at 30,000 ft.

Anyway, I'm back and will have more info and a flyer for the sfraves 
bar-b-q lunch later tonight (no silly, the bbq is next saturday the 26th, 
the *info* comes tonight. Put that tofu back in the fridge.)

jmar. beep.

> 
>         Equinox was all I expected it to be, and more.  It was in a dirty
> little warehouse, the music was mindblowing (especially the sets by Alex
> from Gaia Mantra and James...especially James!), the energy was high, and
> the cover charge was low.  What more do I have to say?  A big thanks to
> Ivan and Lacey for putting on a killer party that took me back to the old
> days of the undergrounds.

> bhg 

I sat out for equinox, late (1:30) and arrived in the candlestick complex
arround 2.  It took me a while to actually find the place, but I eventually
drove down a street when a guy with a BIG orange Dr. suess type hat (!)
Flashed a flash light at me, I started to have a warm fuzzy feeling :)
as I drove intot the yard, the music was Booming out of a fairly large
but delapidated warehouse, I could see the light from some visual machines
ozzing out of rents in the sides of the building, (I started to get amped!)
Upon entry, I found a reasonably large warehouse space, with sheets put up 
against a couple of sides of the walls to project visuals on, (and the visuals
were really nice, including some great oil lamp stuff!!).  The whole setting
tool me back to the "old days" of 2 1/2 - 3 years ago.  The only problem was
NOT ENOUGH PEOPLE WERE DANCING. There was far too much gawking and standing.
(I don't mean standing and grooving, I mean non participatatory standing and
watching) I can't figure out the  reason for this, the music was great, but
the crowd while friendly and nice, just was not committed to getting a groove
going.  I think a lot of recent ravers are spoiled from going to so many
"legal" venues.  They don't realize how lucky they are, that there are so many
high quality parties here and they expect the promoter to "entertain" them and
be totally responsible for the quality of the experience they are having.  Two
years ago every one in that place would be going completely ballistic, feeding
the DJ their energy and dancing for dear life, (cuz they would know that the 
Blue People could be at the door at any moment!) And in fact the Blue People
did shopw up a couple of times, (the Brisnbane cops were fairly cool, the first
couple of times they told them to turn down the music, they didn't seem upset
at us being there but they said they were getting complaints from daily city :)
So at 5:30 they come back during Garth's set, the promoters tell Garth he HAS
to turn it down, Garth seems to get this look on his face like saying "fuck 
all that" and cranks it! (I guess if it is going to be shut down, go out with 
bang, not a whimper :) Any ways the lights come on and the police come in
with a dog ! and clear everybody out, they were fairly nice about it and I saw
a least one group of ravers enlist one of the cops in taking a group picture
of the lot!  SO at 5:30 everyone scattered, not a bad party for $12 and I hope
the equinox people throw another undereground, the scene needs this energy and
expertise because we never know when ALL of our parties might have to be
underground once again.

gangster/hate generation.. it's all to sad that these anger filled upright 
apes with guns are moving in.. what can we do to make are scene unattractive 
to them? i and five friends spent time in SF general because of gang 
violence i still have the scares.! Please THINK about where your next events 
will be at.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From sfraves-owner  Mon Mar 21 12:01:27 1994
Received: by techno.Stanford.EDU (4.1/1.34)
	id AA03564; Mon, 21 Mar 94 12:01:27 PST
Received: from soda.berkeley.edu by techno.Stanford.EDU (4.1/1.34)
	id AA03552; Mon, 21 Mar 94 12:01:15 PST
Received: (laura@localhost) by soda.berkeley.edu (8.6.8/PHILMAIL-1.10) id MAA09799 for sfraves@techno.stanford.edu; Mon, 21 Mar 1994 12:01:11 -0800
Message-Id: <199403212001.MAA09799@soda.berkeley.edu>
From: laura@soda.berkeley.edu (Laura La Gassa)
Date: Mon, 21 Mar 1994 12:01:09 -0800
X-Mailer: Mail User's Shell (7.2.3 5/22/91)
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: "Catwoman" was YUMMY!!!
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Hi all!  I spent part of the weekend in Denver, and thought I'd report on 
how things went there for your entertainment pleasure (hee).

I flew out Saturday afternoon, going to the Mile High City for the first 
time.  All the other times I'd flown coast to coast had been at night, so I 
got to see the Rockies for the first time.  Landing in Denver is impressive: 
you swoop down out of the snow-covered mountains and onto the end of the 
Great Plains -- which are extremely flat.  

My friend Eric McCormick, who used to live in DC, met me at Stapleton (the 
gorgeous new Denver International is still not opened due to bugs in their 
high-tech optically encoded fabulous baggage handling system) with a boquet 
of flowers.  We went back to his very cool apartment, which is actually a 
storefront on a low hill west of downtown, and hung out there for a while.  
Eric makes techno, and played me his newest creation (a tribal/breaky 
trancey piece being shipped to Instinct Records even as we speak).  He also 
showed me the  "fluff piece" he was in on a local Denver newscast about 
Denver musicians that was run before the Grammy Awards.  Best of all Eric 
fed me home-made manicotti, and we gorged ourselves.  After a nighttime tour 
of "Lower Downtown" (including window shopping at Williams-Sonoma and stops 
at two coffehouses) we made our way to the party.

"Catwoman" was held in a small warehouse/loading dock/single truck garage a 
bit southwest of downtown.  It was near a residential area, so I was a bit 
worried, but nothing happened even though the cops dropped by to say hi.
The space was GREAT:  it had that old warehousey industrial feel to it, yet 
still had a nice bathroom, and wasn't all grimey and filthy yet wasn't "too 
clean" for ravers.  It was also heated, which is a plus for parties in a 
city where it was 75 during the day and 38 that night.

The sound system was the right size for the space, and sounded good from the 
floor but was HORRIBLY distorted when heard from where the DJ setup was.  I 
am completely spoiled by Ethan's Liquid Air setup and Bryce's methodical 
tweaking of the system.  But at least it sounded good to the dancers, 
although mixing was a complete nightmare.

The coolest thing about Catwoman was that Eagle (the organizer) took the
time to actually decorate the space.  He had an ingenious rig of little
fluffy clouds made from large painted pieces of posterboard hanging from
the ceiling.  There were about 20 individual clouds, all mounted in this
sort of web of twine, which was then strung across the dance

[ DARN!  I'd written a whole great description here, but when I 
ftp-d it from my work site to soda to post it, half of it got eaten!
and I had already deleted it from the work site.  Doh! ]

area.  Eagle and Leah's (yes, our sfraves / diva / Berkeley pal) friend
Laura created two huge neon-dayglo paintings which were hung on the
walls.  The DJ area was decorated with "Catwoman" birthday party
decorations.  Best of all there were a few lighting effects:  a single
strobe, one intella-beam like thing, and something globe-shaped that
looked like a UFO and spun around emitting beams of colored light.  The
guy running the lights would turn things off and on from time to time to 
vary them according to the mood.

Behind the dance area there was a sort of ante-warehouse that featured
a huge futon, and tables selling soda, snapple, espresso, and smart
drinks.

You'd think with such a brilliant set up the party would be a screaming
success, but due to bad politics in the Denver scene it wasn't.  It
seems that about two weeks after Eagle had announced and started flyering 
for Catwoman, another better-known promoter announced his own party for
the same night.  This other promoter even had people standing in the
parking area outside of Catwoman telling people that they were in the
wrong place, that this was a private party and the one they were looking
for was down the road and across the freeway.  When Eagle found out about 
this he told them to leave, but by then the damage had been done.  I
think Catwoman got about 75 people all night, whereas the other party
had several hundred.

Regardless, Catwoman was BEAUTIFUL.  From the time I dropped the first
record of the night the people there were dancing.  Even people standing
on the edge of the floor talking to their friends were bopping up and down.
I played for an hour and a half, mostly the sort of things I was playing at 
the Blue Cube / Friends and Family, and the energy level in the room 
was very high.  Each person was giving off the energy and vibe of like
five people.   Then Louise took over and gave us all a brilliant ride,
playing everything  from one old disco song to trance bordering on hardcore,
with progressive house and bleepy trance in between.  Louise is from
the UK but is now living in Amsterdam, and she strikes me as being a
European version of Heather Heart.  I haven't had so much fun dancing in a
long time.  Over the course of the night people started leaving, and around
3 am it was looking quite sparse.  I remarked to Eagle that it would
probably be better to end it early while everyone is still happy and has a 
positive image of the party than to let it drag on and die.  He said he'd
see how things went.  So, I started a second set at 3.30 am.  By then
there were only about six people dancing, so at 4 (with only two people
still dancing but the rest hanging out and talking happily) we shut off
the music.

I had such a great time though, the people in Denver at Catwoman were
so friendly, and were a mixed group ranging from very young 
raver-archetypes decked out in stripes and baggies to late 20-something
club goers to older net ravers to newbies.  Every single person had
a smile and many many people talked to me while I was hanging out, telling
me about how they got into raving, and asking me about music and how I
liked Denver.  I haven't been around such a great bunch of strangers since
I was in Montreal nearly a year ago.

I was left with so much happy positive energy from the party that I
didn't sleep that night.  We went back to Eric's and then went up to
the skyscraper where he works to see the sunrise, and I also took a
great Body Shop enhanced shower.  On the airplane that morning on the
way back I talked to a first-time visitor to San Francisco about what
kinds of things he should try on his visit.  When I got home Brian and
I went out for an excursion that started in a hardware store in the 
Haight and ended with us walking to the the summit of Mt. Tamalpais.  In
between we went to Muir Beach and played fetch with some very friendly
dogs.  IT WAS THAT KIND OF PARTY!!!!!!!!!  Yippeeee!  (And no, I 
didn't have any stimulants other than some tea at 5am and some espresso
at noon.)

Eagle will be doing more parties in the future, and I'll probably be
back in Denver sometime in the next few months.

Hugs to Laura (Zzar), Eagle, Eric, Kirby, Bart (the cockatiel who sings
along to trance), Zach, Brian@indigo, the man in the hardware store
who knew what I meant about those little brackets, and that shepard-
mix mutt who kept bringing the stick back.

Laura

book soon (it may already be out) titled INFORMATION WARFARE.

 Having had the pleasure of meeting and talking at length with
Winn, I am of the opinion that he may be on to something here.

I know, everyone has read about it, but I am going to post anyway..
Equinox kicked.  After Jeno's performance at Motion last week and 
my time at Equinox, it looks like things might start improving out here.
We got Equinox pretty damn early, around 11:30, becuase we didn't want to
stay late.  The first DJ seemed to struggle through is set a bit, lots
of budDUMPbuDUMPbuDUMP bass/trainwrecks, but alex of GaiaMantra (right?) was
really cool.  A lot faster than I have heard before, but really damn cool.
James was really brilliant, I agree.  Cool parts?  Well, hearing the
warehouse walls and ceiling rumble with the Bass was cool, the whole place
emanated the music.  The chill zone was fine, I hate too much blue light,
but that's fine, and the smoke machine use was kept to a minimum.  It was a
bit cool, but that's what jackets are for.  It's really too bad more
people didn't show up, especially after Organic got busted and moved to
16th and Harrison.

Oh well. I hope that Equinox throws another party, the same space would be cool, and I hope lots and lots
of people get their tails in gear and go.

Did anyone go to Good housekeeping?  

have a good week...

To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: don't go to Good Housekeeping
X-Sun-Charset: US-ASCII
Content-Length: 3576

unless you want to experience a really nice Sunday morning
afterhours that has a totally loving "family vibe".

Equinox ended early, and the crowd that I thought would eventually end
up at Good Housekeeping vanished.  I know that an hour and a half is a
long wait but I can't figure out where everyone went except either home
(or maybe to organic :) anyway, I got to GH at 6:50 and banged on the
door, jsl let me in and I could see that he was busy,  I offered to
jump in and help any way that I could, so I moved a few tables, placed
some lamps etc.  The space is really nice for an afterhours, It has a
grill up front with a few stools so you can sit in the sun (some people
like sunshine).  Further in, there is a long bar and a nice warm and
cozy room with tables and chairs, (a nice change when you've been
sitting on concrete all night) you can get a nice breakfast for cheap.
I got a veggie omlette with homefries, the omlette was great, the
homefries were too greasy, but for $3.50 it was nice (more homefries
next time, and not greasy one!).  I don't drink coffee but it was
available as well.  Also fruit salad, would be a nice addition, who
wants bacon and eggs after a night of watching walls melt :). There was
great reggae and dub playing but not so loud that you couldn't talk
over, and around 9 a.m. the live jazz trio (or was it a quartet?)
kicked in and this was perfect, I really liked the fact that after a
night of raving, I could get something healthy to eat and kick back
with my friends and hear some mellow music.  But I hear someone saying,
I WANT TO DANCE!! I DON'T WANT MELLOW. For all you tweekers and trance
addicts out there don't worry, Good Housekeeping has the shit for you!
In the back, with PERFECT sound isolation from the front I might add
is  the *SOUND VISION* sound system, the room may not be acoustically
perfect, but it is large enough to comfortably handle I'd say 50 or so
ravers, the dance floor is wood, it is dark but classy with a few
mirrors.  Ethan and Bryce take great pains to tweek the system so that
it sounds GREAT, I tried to give Ethan some feedback (from a trance
addict's point of view) of what it takes in terms of treble, mids and
bass, to send me out and I must say that this system WILL deliver the
goods.  Markie has the chicken pocks (and is under HOUSE ARREST , or is
the word qurantine :) so he couldn't be there this weekend, but I just
CAN'T WAIT to hear Markie turned loose in this room and on that system,
(mutha fuckers will be hanging from the rafters, once markie does them
up in there!)  I can clearly see that folks who just can't get enough,
will be content with this back room.  Now folks you will need to come
early because when the secret gets out, I'm sure this place will fill
up quick and if john is smart, he will stop letting people in BEFORE it
gets too crowded and oppressive.  I must say that if you are tired of
the "tweeker's ball" then check out Good Housekeeping.  I'm sure you
will be plesantly surprised!


				G

Equinox report
==============
   Sorta short,   because other people already reported on this one,
but I wanted to say that this party was exceptional...

   After attending a pot luck party on Sat evening,   we head out 
to try and find Equinox.    The directions seemed a tad vague,   but
after calling the number several times,  I get the idea of where it is.

   Along a dark and isolated stretch of road,  as we were driving
around,  this guy with a flashlight indicates that we must have found it.

   There were NO cars parked on the street anywhere near this location
and if I hadn't seen the flashlight,  I would have driven right past it.

   As we turned into the parking area,   I could hear the familiar "boom
boom".    After parking the car in the back,   we headed into an old rancid
warehouse and was surprised to learn it was only $12.    WOW!!  A real
underground rave...  And what a kickin party it was.    It was really
cool inside,   so I immediatly started dancing and had a glorious time
drawing energy from a super sound system.

   My knee is completly healed now,  and for the first time,   I decided
not to bother with my knee brace,   and ice.    I didn't need any of
these,   because in the last 4 days,   during one of my exercise sessions
I heard my knee snap into place,   after that,  I now got full range
of motion and no more pain.   It's wonderful.  For the first time,
I'm fully recovered from my 4 month ago injury,   even my lower back
never complained,  and I dance my butt off.

   Unfortunately,  after Garth's set,  the pigs shut it down.   Sheesh!
Don't understand what dickwad lives out there so far from everywhere
and got bothered by noise.    Anyway,   after a snafu with the car,  
I head over to Good Houskeeping and hung out there for a while,  and
eventually wound up at the End Up,  still dancing until about 4 pm.
WOW!!  Sure feel great today....  Knee not sore anymore,   and I
did my full exercise set for the first time in 4 months.   I got
lots of catching up to do,    but I think I'll be back to my full
high energetic self by this summer to hace a ravin kickin time...

   I heard Organic got moved to Haze theator...  Anyone go to that?
Haven't heard any reports...

Keep the scene alive..

I have attached a copy of the press release that is going out to several
hundred publications in the next week + introducing the first IICS CD-ROM
Showcase.  Inclusion in this CD-Rom will cost nothing to the participants,
although as is always the case, space is limited.

ATTENTION ALL MULTIMEDIA ARTISTS: Read the press release below and get back
to me asap because the next release will probably not be free to
participants.

"From the seed of personal responsibility, 
blossoms the power to change the world."

Mark Sigal 
(hypermrk@crl.com)

                   IICS ANNOUNCES FIRST CD-ROM SHOWCASE

The International Interactive Communications Society (IICS) has
announced the development of their first IICS Multimedia CD-ROM
Showcase.  The IICS is a 10-year-old international non-profit
organization formed to promote, inform, and represent multimedia
professionals by providing information exchange, education,
networking, and support. The CD-ROM will showcase the diversity
of high quality work being created by multimedia artists,
programmers and developers working across the country to
integrate text, sound, graphics, and video into a whole new range of
applications. 

"While there is a tremendous public awareness of so-called
buzz words like 'interactive' and 'multimedia,' few truly
understand the scope of business, consumer and educational
solutions that stand to be realized by this emerging medium,"
says Chris Ray, president of the San Francisco Bay Area chapter
of IICS.  

"This project aims to elevate the concept of interactive
multimedia to a whole new level by highlighting for both
consumers and business leaders the tremendous communication power generated
by this medium."

In undertaking this project, the IICS believes that the Showcase 
will ultimately become the definitive source for viewing examples
of multimedia and locating development talent for hire.  Hence,
with the aim of reaching the widest possible audience, the IICS
Multimedia Showcase will support both Windows and Macintosh
platforms.

Consistent with the organization's non-profit theme, all sales
proceeds will go towards hiring an Executive Director to oversee
the international organization's rapidly growing membership.

Content for the IICS CD-Rom Showcase is being compiled through a
"CALL FOR ENTRIES" from members only. Selected works are included on the disc
at no cost to submitters. Adds Ray, "We wanted to provide artists an initial
no-cost incentive to come out of the woodwork.  Subsequent releases of the
Showcase will almost
assuredly require submission fees on the part of the artists."

The IICS, founded in 1983, is the premier non-profit organization
for individuals involved in the field of interactive multimedia. 
With over 3,000 members, over 20 chapters worldwide and 100%
annual membership growth, the society brings together individuals
of affiliated industries, and provides a forum for learning about
new technologies, ideas, creative influences, professional
services and information on emerging trends.  For membership 
information on the IICS chapter nearest you, call (503) 579-4427.

To request a CALL FOR ENTRIES form, contact Mark Sigal at
HyperMark@AOL.COM or via the Internet at hypermrk@crl.com or call the San
Francisco chapter at (415) 553-2202.

Don't give up on the forwarded message below until after third paragraph.
Regardless of your culinary preferences, the story is rich for students of
organizational behavior.  I think there's a TQM moral in here someplace.

Howard Rosenberg                      phone: 510/642-7103
University of California, Berkeley    fax: 510/642-6108
>>
>> I received this mail and thought some of you would appreciate a nice
>> cookie receipe.
>>
>>
>>   My daughter & I had just finished a salad at Neiman-Marcus Cafe
>> in Dallas & decided to have a small dessert.  Because our family
>> are such cookie lovers, we decided to try the "Neiman-Marcus
>> Cookie". It was so excellent that I asked if they would give me
>> the recipe and they said with a small frown, "I'm afraid not."
>> Well, I said, would you let me buy the recipe?  With a cute
>> smile, she said, "Yes."  I asked how much, and she responded,
>> "Two fifty." I said with approval, just add it to my tab.
>>
>>   Thirty days later, I received my VISA statement from
>> Neiman-Marcus and it was $285.00.  I looked again and I
>> remembered I had only spent $9.95 for two salads and about $20.00
>> for a scarf.  As I glanced at the bottom of the statement, it
>> said, "Cookie Recipe - $250.00."  Boy, was I upset!! I called
>> Neiman's Accounting Dept. and told them the waitress said it was
>> "two fifty," and I did not realize she meant $250.00 for a cookie
>> recipe.  I asked them to take back the recipe and reduce my bill
>> and they said they were sorry, but because all the recipes were
>> this expensive so not just everyone could duplicate any of our
>> bakery recipes....the bill would stand.  I waited, thinking of
>> how I could get even or even try and get any of my money back.
>>
>> I just said, "Okay, you folks got my $250.00 and now I'm going to
>> have $250.00 worth of fun." I told her that I was going to see to
>> it that every cookie lover will have a $250.00 cookie recipe from
>> Neiman-Marcus for nothing. She replied, "I wish you wouldn't do
>> this." I said, "I'm sorry but this is the only way I feel I could
>> get even," and I will.
>>
>>   So, here it is, and please pass it to someone else or run a few
>> copies....I paid for it; now you can have it for free.
>> (Recipe may be halved.):
>>
>> 2 cups butter                  4 cups flower
>> 2 tsp. soda                    2 cups sugar
>> 5 cups blended oatmeal**      24 oz. chocolate chips
>> 2 cups brown sugar             1 tsp. salt
>> 1  8 oz. Hershey Bar (grated)  4 eggs
>> 2 tsp. baking powder           3 cups chopped nuts
>> 2 tsp. vanilla                        (your choice)
>>
>>   Cream the butter and both sugars.  Add eggs and vanilla; mix
>> together with flour, oatmeal, salt, baking powder, and soda.  Add
>> chocolate chips, Hershey Bar and nuts.
>>   Roll into balls and place two inches apart on a cookie sheet.
>> Bake for 10 minutes at 375 degrees.  Makes 112 cookies.
>>
>> ** measure oatmeal and blend in a blender to a fine powder.
>>
>> Have fun!!!  This is not a joke --- this is a true story..
>> ************************************************************
>>   That's it. Please, pass it along to everyone you know, single
>> people, mailing lists, etc.....
>>
>
>

Equinox was the shit!  Ivan & Lacey have done it again with a great party,
in a great space.  Directions could've used some help but overall a REAL UG
party!  As stated before, it was in a really large warehouse with plenty of
room, plenty of ventillation.  The music was pretty good overall.  Was
sorry to not hear Jeno that night, but James MORE than made up for it!
James fucked it up, playing some really hard trippy shit that had the whole
place moving (I dunno what GeoffW means by people were just standing
around)!  Everytime I hear James recently he keeps getting better, and
better.  '94 has his name written all over it!  He was tellin that tale
with the TT's!  Fuck yeah!

Nice one for Ivan & Lacey, nice one for the community!  Keep it REAL, and
that is exactly what they did!

Good Housekeeping went well.  Special thanks to Ethan and Bryce who have
probably THE best sound system in SF!  They really put alot of heart into
it and it showed!  Overall a fairly good "family vibe", which is exactly
what we wanted to achieve.  The space is really nice for a Sunday morning
thing, and as time goes on will prove to be an excellent venue for those
who want to chill out, or trip out, without all the pagentry.  I was VERY
pleased to see a few of the SFR posse around like Moni, Tom, The Capn', and
Lee Fogel (a real pleasure to finally meet him!).  Thanks for your support!
I also want to thank the crew at 1190 for being great people to deal with!
The live Jazz was kickin' and we will continue with the live music since
that is what we're all about.

There were the usual fumbles, fouls, and foibles that happen during a first
gig.  But these kinks have already been worked out and things will be alot
smoother this next go around.  So if you're hungry and wanna eat, chill
out, or even DANCE, please stop by and say hello.  It's all about THAT!
And keep your eyes peeled since we will usually have two to three guest
spots open for the *newcomers* and veteran TT technicians in the area!
Becuase it's all about THAT!

Also a special thanks to everyone who attended!

Future plans - Looking forward to Ethan & Bryce doing their magic in the
future (is this a blatant hint or what), and booking a wide variety of
fresh female talent.  So get me a tape or let me know when you're playing
next so's I can catch ya' (big hint).

Overall a good weekend.  Time to get some sleep for this Sunday and other
activities (like 20Hz, special edition shirts, etc.).

Pax,
John

I haven't been watching the list very closely, but I'm still pretty
sure that nobody has mentioned the article about techno in the April
issue of Rolling Stone.

Titled, "Welcome to the Machine (The Techno Revolution Comes to Your
Town)", the article opens with a four paragraph descrition of the
Halloween FMR!  The author (Sue Cummings) even refers to "DJ Garth" as
"one of the stars of the bay area rave scene", and the FMR as "one of
the most authentic examples of a ritual that has spread from the West
Coast to other U.S. Cities."

The article goes on about techno and how it is the only music that has
remained 'underground' (rap and punk don't qualify anymore :).  Stuff
on Moby and Orbital too.

Interesting reading because this is from Rolling Stone Magazine, our
national canon of pop/music culture.  Anthony Kiedis on the cover, FMR
on page 15!

In all the journals and texts and other materials I've read on
psychoactives, I've never come across anything that suggested that
psilocin and psilocybin have any long term effects. That doesn't mean
they don't, but it means that if they do, the effects are subtle, or
it's very likely the medical community would have noticed by now.

I'd say it's a safe bet that your average hamburger has far more long
term toxicity than a dose of shrooms.

Subject: William James on raving
Reply-To: rnj%lila@us.oracle.com
