William James, *The Varieties of Religious Experience*, 1902, p 76:

   "If we were to ask the question: 'What is human life's chief concern?' one  
of the answers we should receive would be: 'It is happiness.'  How to gain,  
how to keep, how to recover happiness, is in fact for most men at all times  
the secret motive of all they do, and of all they are willing to endure.  The  
hedonistic school in ethics deduces the moral life wholly from the experiences  
of happiness and unhappiness which different kinds of conduct bring; and, even  
more in the religious life than in the moral life, happiness and unhappiness  
seem to be the poles round which the interest revolves.  We need not go so far  
as to say with the author whom I lately quoted that any persistent enthusiasm  
is, as such, religion, nor need we call mere laughter a religious exercise;  
but we must admit that any persistent enjoyment may *produce* the sort of  
religion which consists in a grateful admiration of the gift of so happy an  
existence; and we must also acknowledge that the more complex ways of  
experiencing religion are new manners of producing happiness, wonderful inner  
paths to a supernatural kind of happiness, when the first gift of natural  
existence is unhappy, as it so often proves itself to be."

	I believe our scene has already overcome the "threat" of 
popularization.  Its been on TV before and in many articles previous to 
this.  And yes we have seen the downsides of popularization with some of 
the huge parties and bad people around here, but as long as there are people 
like us who keep attending the small intimate parties and keep the vibe 
alive, the scene will survive in one form or another.  
	How did you find out about this scene?  I am willing to bet that 
many of us heard about how cool these weird rave things were and a friend 
of yours happened to know when and where some party was gonna be held so 
you went.  Now I realize that a friend telling you where a party is and a 
national magazine reviewing a rave are very different but if it hasn't 
become "too" popular by now I doubt it ever will.
	I really don't see any problem with the popularization of the 
rave scene.  Whats wrong with a bunch of people getting the chance 
to experience a rave and to maybe enlighten their thinking a bit. They 
might get the chance to share the love and family spirit of a rave.  I 
really would not mind if everybody in the world got this chance to feel 
the same thing as we do every time we go to a party.  Wow if you can work 
through the wordiness of that last sentence then you are on the right track.
	Anyway I just wanted to share my thoughts on the popularization 
of the scene.  I know that the practicality of my thinking is low but 
at least it sounds good in theory.  It doesn't hurt to try.  We always 
need to bring new people into the scene to keep it going as we fade out, 
don't be elitist.  You were on the outside at one time too, and now that 
you're "in" don't forget that.  I do understand that making it hard to 
get in does make for a better group but there must be a limit.
	Please rebut any area of my ideas if you deem it necessary.  Two 
(or two hundred) minds are better than one.  You only enhance your 
thinking by comparing it to someone else's.

Peace,

G

Gioni Pasquinelli     pasque@netcom.com		
Do what you can today for tomorrow you may be dead.

For a first time shroom eater I would recommend two to three dried grams.
Also this is an intense experience and will probably be more fruitful if 
you chose an appropriate environment and are in a good mental space and 
ready for some inner exploration. I don't recommend heavey doses of 
schrooms at raves unless they are outdoors and on a deep vibe.

For more in depth info on mushrooms check out any book or tape from 
Terence McKenna. If you would like more info on McKenna or are 
intereseted in forming a study group e-mail me privately and we can talk.

					Ronan

>  i have noticed very measurable effects from mushrooms:

> A musician friend of mine says his timing is off for up to a week after.

For me, the comedown from acied was very hard, and involved a major loss
of physical coordination (no rhythm), not to mention bad aural feedback
in my head and a general feeling of being fucked up, like my body and mind
had been pushed way too hard.  The day after was a bit harsh, too.

Mushrooms, on the other hand, left me with a euphoric feeling of having
come through the fire of an intense experience.  I felt spent, 
but incredibly energized, and didn't experience any long-term adverse
effects.  On the contrary, my spiritual health was greatly enhanced.

Hint:  Mushrooms and man-made environments don't mix well.  Be with
nature in a beautiful place.

Hint 2:  Think of some question or reason you are 'doing mushrooms'.  What
are you looking for?  The mushroom will always come back with an answer, 
if you listen for it -- not as a voice from above but as understanding.

Doing psychedelics as a way to pass time is a bad idea.  If you wish
too hard to be permanently altered you might actually get your wish,
and you will have traded a drab reality for a drab reality with tracers
and fugue states.

// g

Subject: burnout vs toxicity

On witnessing burnout:
	I have known several very bright and knowledgable people
	who were very healthy- emotionally, mentally, and physically,
	whose minds deteriorated with prolonged use of psychadelics.
	I can think of 10 people offhand- including relatives. 
	Most of them either smoked pot every day or took heavy
	psychadelics every weekend.

On post-drug mental states:
	My personal opinion is that hallucinogens force more input to
	the mind than it is designed for. For some this can produce a
	fine "broken-in" effect like broken in shoes- well worn and
	perfect fit. 
	For others it seems to make them very intelligent- ever known
	anyone who was a stoner and great student who had endless appetites
	for studying? My heavy pot user friends and I came up with the
	reason for this: heavy pot use destroys your minds ability to
	multitask. With heavy use you become less *distracted* during
	non-stoned times because you *aren't* multitasking. Under these
	conditions its far easier to be a great student, programmer,
	or whatever else you do that requires concentration.

My personal observations:

	I used to be a very angry and argumentative person. I set out
	on a mission to "burn" this part of my mind out by overdriving
	it enough to destroy the endless desire for conflicts thate I seemed
	to have. After several doses of mushrooms and pot I got the 
	exact results. However along with that came a slight tint of apathy-
	kind of a slacker attitude.

Just because psychadelics aren't toxic doesn't mean that they don't have
long term effects. I would suggest to anyone who plans to try mushrooms,
LSD, E, Opium, Peyote, PCP that they very carefully think through what they
are doing before because they may very well come out a different person
after the experience.

Infrequent pot use doesnt' seem to have any real effects- however my pot
use was a very very intense concentrated (thc extract) one.

My advice for using mushrooms (stemming from personal experience only):

Take care of yourself nutritionaly, be well rested (REM sleep releases
neurochemicals essential for mental balance), avoid stimulants (caffiene
in particular), be with people you know and love, and don't do anything
you don't feel comfortable with.  I did not do these things once 
and suffered pretty bad consequences.  I was more or less cooked for
about a month afterwards, had to drop out of school because I couldn't
leave the house alone (no joke).  I eventually went to the doctor and
he determined that through a combination of things (not the mushrooms
alone) I temporarily threw off my neurochemistry.  He was able to
treat my physiological imbalances but the psychological trauma followed
me for a year+/- afterwards.  Three years later I still suffer from
an occasional anxiety attack.  These attacks are purely psychological
ususally triggered off when something reminiscent of the experience
occurs.  As time has passed they seem to happen less frequently
and I imagine soon I will be rid of them completetly.  

By telling this story I'm not trying to scare anyone away from
using mushrooms or any other substance for that matter.  Prior
to this experience I had used mushrooms for about a year with no
ill effects, quite the contrary, I loved them.  I had wonderful
times with them and learned so much about life, people and myself. 
They were really helpful to me in a number of ways, and even the
above experience was very educational and I wouldn't change a thing
about it.  I look back now and laugh at some of the weird shit
that went on in my head.  :)  I was lucky though, I had *extremely*
supportive family and friends.  I've seen others that don't
have the same support network as I do go through experiences similar
to mine and they did not come through as well as I did.

Much of the ingredients in the get well recipe that my doctor
perscribed me are avaliable at health food stores, if anyone
is interested drop some email my way.  Now as a matter of course
I take the supplements after any psychedelic type experience and
am usually less spun afterwards (if not completely normal) than 
those with me that don't take them.  (Could be a psychosomatic
response, but hey if it works...)

Take care,
CC
-- 
Candice			pandora@hulk.sfsu.edu


    I'm nothing now, but I'm something compared to what I used to be.

From: Jeremy Greenwood <jgreenw@extro.ucc.su.OZ.AU>:

The best medical evidence would suggest no long-term toxicity associated
with psiloc(yb)in. Anecdotal evidence would suggest that the effects of
this drug are less likely to cause short term adverse reactions than
"harder" psychedelics such as LSD and DO*. Most users report less
post-session fatigue after psiloc(yb)in than most other psychedelics,
and certainly less than for many of the phenethylamines. The dangers
of chronic repeated ingestion are of course unknown, but it would
be reasonable to assume that the brain will readjust and compensate
under this kind of stress, (i.e. receptor populations might change
and their function might be down/upgraded). This would translate into
differences in the unintoxicated brain, but whether or not these 
differences would be of any significance is unknown. Such changes in
the biases of the mechanics of the brain could also be expected to
be reversible once the exposure was discontinued. Certainly there
are no reports of major neurological change associated with the use
of psilocin. However, it should be noted that psychedelics often
exacerbate the symptoms of schizophrenics and other mentally imbalanced
people, including those with borderline psychoses, and thus such
people should be discouraged from using such substances, particularly
on a regular basis.

In essesnce, psilocin is as safe as any recreational drug could ever
be expected to be. It is very similar to endogenous compounds, and
as such is easily dealt with by the body and the brain.

Jeremy

(Feel free to add this to the discussion if you think it would be of
interest to people.)

                   "Enjoy moderation in moderation"

From: csc@pilot.njin.net (Sean Casey)
Message-Id: <9403240437.AA23263@pilot.njin.net>
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: burnout vs toxicity
In-Reply-To: <199403240210.SAA07603@mail.netcom.com>
References: <199403240210.SAA07603@mail.netcom.com>
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

I suspect that long term changes with most psychedelics are due to
psychological and not physiological phenomena.  Likely exceptions are
THC and MDMA; more study is needed.  Overdoing any activity is a good
way to bring about negative change. One needs to keep a good balance.

Also, don't overlook those who use drugs to escape depression or other
problems. There is a strong correlation then between heavy drug use
and negative personal change, but one needs to see the whole picture.

At one time in my life, computers were my escape. My focus became
laser-sharp, my ability to accomplish things was phenomenal.  But
everyday life dropped away into a haze. I stopped taking care of
myself, my depression deepened. I lived only to be on the computer,
spinning stuff in my head into computer programs on the screen.

Well I survived, but make no mistake, if it weren't computers, it
would have been something else. And my behavior to other people was
very unfocused and unreal, not unlike a major "pothead".

Perhaps the best thing to do is more studies of people in certain drug
use patterns. Then we'll know.

One of the interesting things about MDMA is it's entirely likely that
heavy use over long periods of time causes a certain amount of long
term damage to the seratonergic system. And yet those who have used
over a long period of time show the exact opposite kinds of changes
one would expect with this sort of damage.  The users report being
happier, more open, and less aggressive. 

But as Steve said, one should think carefully before doing
psychoactives. It is serious stuff; one should consider the reasons
one wishes to try them, and consider one's own state of mind.

Sean

	ALL OF THIS INFORMATION IS MY ****OPINION***** ONLY!
	IT IS NOT SCIENTIFIC FACT OR ANY OTHER FACT. USE AT YOUR
	OWN RISK.


	heres my opinion on how to choose if drugs r 4 u.

	do you feel *fear* of taking them? if so then DONT.
	if you are a bit nervous thats one thing- but FEAR is a sign
	that you should not be trying this stuff out.

	do you feel comfortable in large crowds? this is a sign
	that you may do well with drugs. large crowds make a person
	vulnerable physically yet also are very intense and stimulating.
	if you enjoy large crowds and feel comfortable like this then
	this is an indicator that drugs *may* work well for you.

	do you have a history of mental illness in you family? if you
	do then i would seriously recommend drugs. they may be the
	catalyst....

	do you feel that you can gain a large amount of knowledge or
	experience from drugs? if you do then drugs are NOT for you.
	knowledge and experience, in large quantities, come from simply
	LIVING and gettin out there in the world. drugs are an *enhancer*.
	they are a *tool* for interpreting things in a different way- they
	are NOT a golden ray of light streaming into your mind and teaching
	you. if thats what you are looking for then you may consider getting
	into religion- but not drugs.

	and most importantly: do you feel that you have a great deal of
	control in your life? if so than when put to the test- when you
	are incapacitated, then you will do better than people who feel
	very vulnerable all the time. however if you are a control-fiend
	then you may not do so well with drugs. control-fiends usually have
	problems when they realize that they no longer have control.

	Read Substance D by Phillip K Dick. the best book about drugs
	I've ever read.

-------------------------------------------------------------

1-3 grams are a good "introdutory" dose, after that take it from there.

Read any standard description of a psychedelic experience and that will give
you an idea of the possibilites but they realy are endless.  Also add to
that description a possible slight feeling of nausea at first although it's
also not uncommon for some people to feel more than a slight feeling or to
throw up (but than it's usualy over and they feel great).  

You could have a wonderful time at a rave or a not so good one.  Try it in
a more controlled environment for your first time.

Picking up on a previous thread, I noticed the following event at
Stanford University that might be interesting to some of you.  What
does this have to do with SF-Raves?  Well, I guess if the Clinton

                     ENCRYPTION AND DIGITAL COMMUNICATIONS:
                          LAW ENFORCEMENT OR PRIVACY?

                            An Oxford-Style Debate


                     J. Kent Walker, Jr. (Stanford Law '87)
        Assistant U.S. Attorney and Coordinator, High-Tech Task Force

                       Marc Rotenberg (Stanford Law '87)
     Washington Director, Computer Professionals for Social Responsibility


                       Wednesday, March 30, 1994, 5:30 PM
                         Stanford Law School, Room 290
                           Light Refreshments Served


This debate brings together two nationally prominent experts in this
area.  You won't want to miss the verbal fireworks and the
opportunity to learn more about this important question.

Background
==========

The Clinton Administration is promoting use of the Clipper Chip
technology that provides encryption, but in a form that law
enforcement can unscramble. It also backs legislation requiring
design of digital communications networks so ongoing surveillance
will be feasible.

Law enforcement officials argue that these proposals are necessary
to protect society from criminals and preserve important
investigative tools.

Privacy advocates contend that these proposals grant broad new
powers to law enforcement agencies and diminish protection for
future users of the National Information Infrastructure.
Sponsored by the Stanford Law and Technology Policy Center and the
Stanford Law and Technology Association.

Additional Information
======================

Contact the Stanford Law and Technology Policy Center by email
(Law.Tech.Policy@forsythe) or telephone (415-725-7788).

cc:  GR.CLG

I'm no expert, but the best info I've found so far is:

1-2 medium fresh shrooms
1-3 grams of dried shrooms (far less potent)

I think the low end of this dosage will give you a pretty solid trip,
so beginners should start there. Or less if it makes you nervous.

Doing a lot of mushrooms can take you way WAY out there. Have a
tripsitter. Fortunately, you come down a lot faster than with LSD
(which can be annoying at times).

Sean

>	My personal opinion is that hallucinogens force more input to
>	the mind than it is designed for. 

My personal opinion has always been more like the opposite of this.  
I think hallucinogens make you dumb, so "dumb" that the obvious becomes
revelatory.  This insight or vision of your more basic levels of
functioning can be very new and exciting or scary or funny.

Advice - 2 grams can be *strong* depending on the mushrooms.  I know lots
of people who took 1 gram (or less) for the first time.

It's all you baby, and your state of mind.  Be comfortable.

I think it is very social - do it with friends.
Lower doses with buddies can make you feel like a special little group
exploring a goofy new place together.

I disagree with the "nature connection" just because it is organic.
That seems like a fine trip (Huxley?) but certainly isn't the only one.
If big man-made things bug you then avoid them.  
It is not the drug it is you.

Dave

>	do you have a history of mental illness in you family? if you
>	do then i would seriously recommend drugs. they may be the
>	catalyst....

my guess is that this is a typo.  if you have a history of mental
illness, you should definitely NOT do psychoactive drugs.

i have two good friends who both have a history of mental illness in
the family, both of whom ended up in mental hospitals for a while
after LSD usage.  one case was prolonged usage along with pot, the
other case involved occasional weekend usage over a period of a couple
years.

i'm not trying to panic anyone, just the facts.  my mom is a mental
health professional (20 years, currently supervising Western State
Hospital in Steilacoom WA) and has seen that in many cases,
psychoactives can "unmask" underlying personality disorders,
especially schizophrenia.  (official research pointers, anyone?)

that all said, i have literally dozens of friends who have engaged in
psychoactive drug use and have been very happy with the insights
gained.

as usual, just another monkey pushing the little buttons,
Bob

Subject: mushrooms: locations & doses
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU (sfraves)
Date: Thu, 24 Mar 1994 12:13:50 -40962758 (PST)
X-Mailer: ELM [version 2.4 PL23alpha]

Content-Type: text/plain; charset=US-ASCII
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit
Content-Length: 1568      
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU



Locations:

The only place not to take a psychedelic is someplace
that you don't want to be at.  If you are happy where you
are than the location should be fine.  One of my more
memorable experiences was in a friend's house.  Definate man
made environment but a place I was very comfortable in.
Due to the lack of new stimulation the experience was much
more halucinatory and also more social.

Doses:

This is *really* subjective.  Body weight, empty stomach vs full
stomach, and all of that.  It also depends on ones current
mental state.  Not to mention the age of the mushrooms, what soil
were they grown in, have they been travelling (temperature extremes
(I've heard) affects potency).  But for the sake of not seeming
too vague I'd have to agree with whoever it was that suggested
starting at 1/3 of an 8th for the first time.  If one has had
previous psychedelic experience a higher starting point should be
fine.  But don't bring expections into the trip based on past 
experience with other drugs.  I've seen that throw people for a loop.
Different drug=different experience.  Sounds simple, but it's
easily forgotten.  I've also found with mushrooms that more does
not necessarily mean better.  Although it can, but sometimes more
just means nausea.

All of the above is IMO only.  But after the not so pleseant experience
that I've already told you all about I did do some research in
order to find out exactly what had happened. 

Take care,
CC
-- 
Candice			pandora@hulk.sfsu.edu

The number of grams also depends on the freshness and strain of shroom 
you're taking. I rec 2-3 if you want to have a real intro to the realm of 
psychedelia. Shroom guru and philospher Terence McKenna suggests doing a 
heroic dose of 5grams to really tap into the Gaian Mind. Of course the 
final decision should be on the part of the injestor

Subject: Re: PHILOS - singularity 

Regarding Terence McKenna.

Bibliography

The Invisible Landscape - 1975?  	Seabury Press NY
(This is an analysis of the King Wen sequence of the I Ching. This 
knowledge was revealed to Terence during an extended high bandwidth 
connection with the GAIAN MIND in the early '70's in Central America. 
This work forms the basis of his Timewave Zero theory which deal with the 
ingression of novelty and the end of HIStory in 2012 (coincedentally? also 
the end of the Mayan calendar)

Mushroom Growers Guide- (With Dennis McKenna)	?
(Published under a pseudonym in late '70's early '80's. Require botanical 
skills and could be detrimental to your well being in Police State America)

The Archaic Revival- 		Harper S.F.1991
(This is the best intro to Mckenna's thought. It is a collection of 
articles and talks from various mags and lectures. The text could have 
been edited a bit better but it is still a pleasure to read and packed 
with compelling stories/information/knowledge.)

Food Of The Gods-	? 1992
(This is a radical history of the relationship between psychedelic plants 
and the evolution of conscioussness.)

Trialogues At The Edge of The West: Chaos Creativity and The 
Resacrilization of the World (w/ Rupert Sheldrake & Ralph Abraham)
(This text is highly recommended. A very interesting discussion between 
three of the most important and hopeful contemporary thinkers.)
Bear & Co., Santa Fe 1992

True Hallucinations		Harper S.F. 1993
(This should be read like literature. It is a rant. Not his best text but 
worthwhile none the less.)

Sound Video

I recommend the Space/Time Continuum CD. Very good intro which I find 
entertaining. The video is the shit!!! very well done & "trippy"
Available from Rose X Media House S.F. email me for more info)
There is also a film version available. It is playing in S.F. now tell 
your local independent cinema to pick this up.

My Two Cents On T.M.

Many people try to discredit Terence by saying he's a wacked out crazy 
druggy.Well he is not. He is a very talented philosopher and poet who is 

trying to help our species wake up and celebrate the wonder of chaos and 
gnosis instead of annhilating eachother in a patriarchal bloodbath of 
ecological degradation, social decay and political violence.

I'm open for further discussion and would be interested in starting a 
small study group in the Bay Area.

						Ronan Hallowell
					dada epistemologist/DJ


"Imagine if every problem were solved appropriately, if every 
relationship evolved appropriatedly, if every act were an appropriate 
one. That alone would be the kingdom of heaven. And that is,I think, what 
we're pushing toward. Not cosmic fireworks or the descent of alien beings 
in flying saucers but simply apporpriate activity - EMPOWERED FELT 
EXPERIENCE and the abandonment of the illusion of separateness." -T.M.

I was at a club the other day and I asked the person at the door how to 
have a fun weekend.  The person at the door said that would be two-fifty
and I charged it to my Visa (being at the mythical club which takes 
credit cards).  When I got my Visa bill I found out the info was not
$2.50 but $250, so to get my money's worth I'm going to share the info
with all of you...

Mix the following:
1/2 cup ambience
1       full moon
1 plate spuds n stuff from Good Housekeeping
1/8     House (actually 1 Eighth House)
2       BBQ Tofu
1       additional ingredient of your choice.

Bake for as long as you want.  Do not sleep till finished. ;)

I don't see how we can talk about raving and not talk openly about
drugs, because for most, at one time or another, it is part of the
experience. And a lot of clue needs to be passed around about these
substances, what they do, and how to not get bitten.

The gopher archive at techno is a wonderful resource, and I highly
recommend people go there for detailed information. At the same time,
it's good to get live reports and people's opinions on things.

I'm emphatically on record as saying "raving is not about drugs".
Drugs are NOT the point. But they are, for a lot of people, part of
the experience. Might as well acknowledge that.

Sean

TALES FROM THE MONTEREY RAVE POSSE........Last week, on a note taken from
sfraves, Forrest and I adventured out to "Motion" to see Rick Preston and
Jeno. A singularly cosmic evening was had by all, and driven by Jeno-Energy I
fired through work, teaching my ass off and Shakespeare's. 

Armed with the knowledge that Rick would be playing THIS Wednesday at Motion,
I stayed late a work, and planned for another mid-week fix of rave juice.
Driving from Monterey to SJ, I cranked a Rick Preston tape taken from a
summer Groove Kitchen, and prepared myself.

When I got there, Rick was already finishing his set!!! He decided to play
the One spot, and let DJ Tara, play number Two, before Spun, thus giving her
more exposure and spotlight. She had been billed to play number One. It was a
 genuinely magnanimous offering  on Rick's part, so I couldn't be upset about
missing his set again. (BTW, I drove from Monterey to Sonoma for the Vision
Rave last summer, only to find out Rick had already played.) Besides, DJ Tara
turned out to be a great surprise!

Although some of the seams were a little uneven, and the energy drooped in a
few places, Tara's set was a good mix of tribal, house and acid-jazz. It was
great to see her looking up, smiling, and checking to see how everyone was
doing, and making eye contact. She looked like she was enjoying herself,
dancing a little between those mechanical DJ motions, even though their were
a few tentative traces of fear. But, the crowd responded, and the music
happened. And since this was my second time at Motion, and my first time with
a female DJ, I didn't even notice that the dance floor is still slanted!!!
Next week at Motion is TONY, and the following week is GARTH, so look for
continuing tales from the Monterey Rave Posse...

By the by.....about the Mushroom, I noticed, since resuming after a 10 year
hiatus, that my Mush-E-Room cocktails are the best. However, now that I'm
older (42) the pleasures I take are more in the moment and physical, but
regrets and fears are rooted more deeply in ideas and in the past.
Robertj.......MRP...
"I've got happy feet...."

Hmmm perhaps I better clarify. Drying shrooms decreases their potency
by at least half, mostly because the psilocin--which is even more
psychoactive than the psilocybin--is unstable and readily oxidizes.
Therefore the same shrooms do less for you once dried.

Now while drying shrooms makes them 2-3 times less potent, it also
reduces their weight by a factor of about 100, making dried shrooms
FAR more potent on a weight-by-weight basis.

Sean

/*
 *  the following material is part of some research and writing on raves
 *  i'm doing with a few other folks.  i sent an early draft to brian last 

 *  month; he enthusiastically suggested i share it with sfraves.
 *  corrections, criticisms, and other feedback gratefully received...
 */

RAVE SOCIALIZATION AND INDUCTION
draft e 18 Feb 94  Copyright (c) 1994 by Robert Jesse

Raves had their beginnings as outgrowths from nightclub social gatherings 1  
singles dance clubs, "acid house parties", high energy gay dance clubs, etc.   
These early outgrowth events, proto-raves, were generally modest-sized  
celebrations created by and shared among friends, not for profit, held in  
non-commercial spaces or outdoors.  Not being intended to "draw a crowd"  
beyond the first circle of friends, they were not publicized.

In order to understand how proto-raves grew into the kinds of events now  
called raves, it is necessary to understand the social atmosphere that evolved  
at the early events, how this emergent social atmosphere differed from  
available alternatives, what people valued about the experience, and how  
newcomers were inducted into the scene.
 

Proto-raves were, in outward form, similar to nightclub events , with loud  
dance music, dancing, beverages, social interaction, and sometimes psychedelic  
drugs.  However the social environment and interactions at proto-raves were  
markedly different from those at an ordinary nightclub.  In order to make this  
contrast as clear as possible, we intentionally present perhaps an extreme  
view of "ordinary" non-rave nightclub phenomena.  There is, of course, a great  
variety to be found in nightclubs as well as "raves".

At ordinary nightclubs, many implicit and explicit rules of social conduct  
apply, perhaps more than in most of daily life:  There may be a dress code,  
enforced at the door.  Are you of the right race, age, sexual orientation, and  
socioeconomic stratum to "belong" in this place?  Club-goers expend  
considerable psychic energy in appearing desirable, hip, and cool.  They  
monitor their behaviors for compliance with local norms for how to stand, hold  
a drink, scan the room, move, and interact.   


Complex protocols apply to interactions as simple as eye contact.   Looking at  
somebody of the opposite sex (in a heterosexual environment) may well be  
interpreted by the target as a sexual overture; returning such a glance is an  
early sign of reciprocated interest.  A male must avoid eye contact with  
unknown males, lest it be taken, with immense discomfort, as a homosexual  
advance .  Dancing without a partner in most clubs is discouraged as "weird,"  
and while two or more heterosexual females may be permitted to dance in a  
group, males must never do so.  Dance styles are constrained within  
"acceptable" limits, neither too fast nor too slow, too animated nor too dull.    
Dancers imitate each other rather than allow a personal style to emerge  
creatively.

With all these standards of conduct, one fears "mistakes" (violations of  
convention), occasionally makes "mistakes", and expends more energy in anguish  
over them.  Still more energy goes into forcing a confident smile to cover  
one's uneasiness.   It is easy to see how some nightclub goers might not  
really have much spontaneous, genuine fun (they say, though, that they're  
"having a great time!").   Of those who seem at ease, many of them are  
enjoying the process of acting out the role expected of them, rather than  
enjoying the natural expression of their true selves.  Indeed it is difficult  
even to discover a true self in a society that makes self-expression risky and  
rewards the acting out of a few, approved roles instead. 


The nightclub environment becomes more tense when some people deliberately  
manipulate others in attempts to "pick up" partners, fostering distrust and  
defensiveness.  Add to this the widespread use and abuse of alcohol,  
potentiating male aggressive behaviors, violence, and promiscuity.  It is not  
surprising then that in crowded nightclubs, under great peer scrutiny, users  
of LSD and similar psychedelics occasionally have unpleasant experiences.

Though difficult to document, it seems likely that the incorporation of MDMA  
into private house parties and into the nightclub scene generated the seed for  
the contrasting social environment that emerged in raves.  Users of MDMA  
typically feel a profound safety, love of self, and unconditional positive  
regard for others.  From this self-secure base, it is natural to drop  
pretense.  MDMA users smile and emit other signs of acceptance and  
appreciation to those around them, rewarding others in their expressions of  
self.  These effects are reinforced by music (see below) designed to  
facilitate ecstatic dancing and altered states of consciousness, and sometimes  
by visual images suggesting themes of love, acceptance, global awareness and  
stewardship.

In a setting with some critical mass of MDMA users, the climate changes  
sufficiently so that even those not under the influence of MDMA are drawn into  
the new social patterns ("contact high").  Eye contact and smiles shared  
between strangers are no longer necessarily the beginnings of the mating  
ritual; they can be seen simply as shared expressions of fun. 


MDMA's tactile enhancement rewards physical contact, and the sense of safety  
makes human touch non-threatening.  Thus people who do not share romantic  
interest can enjoy hugs and hand-holding without concern over  
inappropriateness.  Convincing evidence of this is seeing heterosexual males  
show friendliness towards each other physically, acts all the more remarkable  
for occurring in the age groups where homophobia is usually strongest.  These  
behaviors among ravers extend outside raves and to times when they are not  
under the influence of MDMA.

MDMA's enhancement of the sense of proprioception makes physical movement 1  
dance 1 feel wonderful, and the drug's enrichment of audition makes rhythm and  
music seductive.   With no peer expectations regarding style, a heightened  
sensation of physical grace, the pleasure of movement, and smiles from others  
rewarding original expression, dance can induce ecstatic joy.   The endorphins  
released by sustained exercise reinforce this feeling.

Electronic mail (to "sfraves") and other personal accounts document the claims  
of many ravers that especially good rave experiences are among the most  
rewarding experiences of their lives.  Some say that raves have permitted for  
them an unprecedented blossoming of self,  and that the "rave culture"  
supports their ongoing spiritual development.

It is this unburdening, this freedom of being, this unfettered fun, that  
ravers cite so often as a major attraction to the rave scene.  It is probably  
what the proto-ravers told their friends about, and why some of those friends  
asked to be taken to the next rave.  Such word-of-mouth (or electronic mail)  
publicity and personal guidance was the only means of growth for the rave  
scene while raves remained "underground" - unadvertised, on unpredictable  
dates, and at unpredictable locations.

When an experienced raver introduces a friend to the scene, the newcomer may  
receive practical advice on the time and duration of the upcoming rave,  
appropriate adjustment or allocation of sleep time, safe and effective use of  
psychedelics, transportation logistics, etc.  Perhaps more importantly, the  
newcomer will know that he or she will be welcomed as-is, regardless of race,  
gender, age, sexual orientation, "hipness," etc.  Choice of shoes and clothing  
is best dictated by comfort and playful expression of style, rather than by a  
requirement to "fit in".  The standard for behavior is nothing more  
complicated than "be nice to people" (and perhaps that alcohol consumption is  
discouraged or prohibited).  With new ravers suitably prepped, the social  
environment at the rave is reinforced by their addition rather than diluted.

These expectations at the outset and the "good vibe" transmitted by so many  
friendly smiles probably account for the surprisingly low reported incidence  
of  harmful psychedelic experiences at raves.  Good psychedelic experiences  
are further supported by the presence of  "chillout rooms" where it's OK to  
rest and be alone or with a comforting friend when one is feeling overwhelmed,  
and by the freedom to dance alone and refocus the mind (perhaps with eyes  
closed) away from troublesome thoughts by merging consciousness with the  
steady rhythm on the dance floor.

As reported by some organizers in San Francisco, raves emerged from  
underground thus:  The "circles of friends" outgrew what most homes or small  
spaces could accommodate.  As raves moved into larger venues, they became more  
time consuming and expensive to produce (rent, security, DJs, sound,  
lighting).  As capital investment increased, it became necessary to recover  
costs through admission and other charges (coat check, bar, concessions, etc.)   
First the alternative press, and later the mainstream media, began covering  
raves.

As interest grew, more producers came onto the scene to meet the demand.  The  
primary intention of many remained simply to provide the highest quality  
experience possible while not losing much money.  Other producers saw an  
opportunity for considerable profit (a medium-large commercial rave attended  
by 3,000 people may gross $60,000 or more, and net well over two-thirds of  
that).

Producers need a critical mass of people at their events for them to be fun  
(to "go off"), to not loose money, or to satisfy income goals.  In the face of  
competition, promotion becomes necessary for success.   Most commonly,  
promotion of upcoming raves is done by distributing colorful handbills (often  
containing psychedelic art and language) at raves, at nightclubs, in cafes,  
record stores, and clothing stores.  Some producers build up address lists for  
direct mail promotion, and for large raves ("massives" or "megaraves", often  
on holidays, e.g. new years eve or fourth of July), advertisements have been  
run in newspapers and on radio.  These promotions often extend far into  
outlying suburbs and neighboring cities, and often reach quite young age  
groups.

A result of wide promotion is that some of the new ravers attending megaraves  
are no longer personally introduced to the scene by an experienced raver.   
Their expectations are perhaps those of the nightclub scene that raves  
superficially resemble, or those engendered by press, TV, and movie depictions  
of so-called "raves".  In any event, unguided newcomers are generally not well  
prepared to be able to relax their socially conditioned defenses and  
contribute positively to "the vibe" described above.   Large numbers of  
unaccustomed people standing on the sidelines diffuse the ecstatic energy of  
those who are participating in the dance ritual.  At worst, use of alcohol or  
other "downer" drugs and the old nightclub behaviors can quench the vibe that  
distinguishes raves from nightclub events.

In "sfraves" electronic mail discussions and in personal interviews, "old  
time" ravers often express diminishing satisfaction with large commercial  
raves.  A movement appears solidly underway to recreate the lost vibe by  
moving the focus back to smaller, non-commercial raves thrown by friends for  
friends.

Still, ravers report that the feelings of a megarave that "goes off"  
successfully are overwhelmingly positive 1 the ecstasy of merging with  
thousands of people, forming a pulsing, vibrant and joyful mass of humanity.


MUSIC AT RAVES AND ITS EFFECTS

Ravers regard music as one of the central, defining elements of raves.  The  
style heard at raves falls under the general label of "House Music" or simply  
"House".  To the uninitiated, House may sound "all the same".  To musically  
aware ravers and to House musicians, however, there is as much diversity in  
House as in Classical music or Jazz.

Evidence of this is the number of subgenres of House recognized, described,  
and debated by House musicians and ravers:  Chicago House, Deep House, Acid  
House, Techno House (further divided into Proto-Techno, Detroit Techno,  
Hardcore Techno, and Techno-Rave), Breakbeat [House], Hip-House, Trance  
[House], Tribal House, Progressive House,  and Ambient [House].  "House" may  
be used to cover all of these categories, or sometimes among the cognoscenti,  
the word is used as an abbreviation for Chicago House (historically the first  
form of House).  Also played at some raves is Acid Jazz, danceable though  
perhaps not strictly speaking House.

What most characterizes House music (in the broad sense) is its relentless  
devotion to an ongoing beat.  Compared with other styles of dance music,  
melody and lyrics in the usual sense are largely absent.   The music is  
predominated by patterns of rhythm and tone, repeating in cycles of 2, 4, 8,  
..., and shifting over time.  In this sense, House music resembles modern  
"Minimalist" classical music, as typified by composers Terry Riley, Steve  
Reich, and Philip Glass.   Unlike Minimalist music, however, House is nearly  
always constrained to 4/4 time, and House often employs synthesized sounds  
that do not mimic acoustic musical instruments.  House, especially Acid,  
Techno, Trance, and Ambient, often incorporates samples of atonal sounds such  
as voice or sound effects.  These samples, themselves repeated rhythmically,  
may be digitally altered to produce novel or "trippy" effects.  Ambient House  
is distinguished from all other forms of House by its subdued or absent beat.   
Soft in nature, it is often played in in "chillout" rooms to guide the  
relaxing raver in wanderings of the mind.

These categories and descriptions are probably less useful than they seem,  
because variations, exceptions, and evolving styles are the rule.   
Nonetheless, this may give the reader a sense for the evolving diversity of  
House.  Note also that there are strong geographic differences among styles of  
House played at raves at any given time.

Most House music is released by small record companies on 12" vinyl records,  
and sold in specialty dance music stores.  A much smaller number of titles are  
released on CDs.   Since about 1992, House has gained sufficiently in  
popularity so that compilations of House tracks by various artists are now  
available in mainstream record stores as well.
 

Much House music is created for the express purpose of facilitating listeners  
and especially dancers in achieving altered states of consciousness.   
Different styles of House create correspondingly different effects on dancers,  
and consequently are an important control variable for the  "energy" and mood  
at a rave.

Rave DJs are evaluated and admired for their knowledge and skill in thus  
manipulating the crowd and facilitating "the vibe."  A DJ will often play two  
records at the same time, with beats carefully kept in synchronization.   
"Beat-mixing" from one record to the next lets the dance rhythm continue  
unbroken.  Respected DJs are sensitive to the state of the dancers, and will  
guide them on a ride through different moods during the event.  To generalize:   
Chicago House, with its uplifting vocal samples and happy piano riffs,  
increases the energy, induces smiles, and promotes social interaction on the  
dance floor.  Techno House, with its still more intensely pounding rhythms,  
rapid tempos, and frequently harsh sounds, drives the dance energy to manic  
levels.  Breakbeat keeps the energy high, while its more complicated rhythms  
induce ravers to move with more complex dance steps.  Trance is a calmer style  
with less differentiated beats, conducive to closed-eye trance dancing,  
sometimes reducing social interaction on the dance floor.  Tribal, borrowing  
from African and other "world music" rhythms, similarly encourages  
inner-directed states of consciousness which many experience as primal.

The styles of House are related to the states of consciousness that some  
ravers explore using psychedelic drugs.  Thus House music is regarded by some  
ravers as drug music.  Many ravers report, however, that they learn from  
psychedelic experiences how to attain beneficial or enjoyable states of  
consciousness by music and dance alone 1 without chemical assistance.

Many ravers note the historical connections of the social mixture of music,  
optionally psychedelics, and dance, to the tribal celebrations found in  
ancient cultures, often spiritual or religious in nature, and to the spiritual  
practices of the Whirling Dervishes.   Some ravers explicitly regard their  
rave experiences as spiritual or religious exercise.

Note on Music Volume

In common with dance music as played at ordinary night clubs, House music at  
raves is often played at high volume.  Ravers report two benefits from  
powerfully loud music.  First, the synthesized bass sounds can be felt on and  
in the body, adding another sensory mode to the rhythmical experience.   
Second, the volume of the music can overwhelm experience such that the raver  
feels lost in the music and can more easily achieve hypnotic or other altered  
states of consciousness.

The clear disadvantage is that the sound is loud enough at some events to  
damage hearing.  This potential is exacerbated when ravers ("speaker  
tweekers") dance directly in front of a loudspeaker stack, and when exposure  
is many hours in duration.

A small but growing minority of ravers are observed wearing earplugs.   A few  
San Francisco rave producers make disposable earplugs available at their  
events at no cost.  And, some 1993 Internet email to "sfraves" has discussed  
volume measurements taken at raves, sound system quality and safety, and has  
provided ordering information for disposable earplugs in quantity at low cost  
(under twenty cents a pair).


OTHER SENSORY COMPONENTS IN THE RAVE ENVIRONMENT

Lighting:  computer controlled "articulate lighting", strobes, blacklights,  
candles in chillout rooms.

Images:  projected from slide, overhead, or movie projectors.   multiple  
sources combined, like House tracks combined by the DJs.

Video:  computer-generated or computer-manipulated images, often as a  
real-time performance by a video artist.  concrete images, abstract images.   
themes of peace, earth, love, ecology, childlike innocence, the cosmos, etc.

Scents:  sites sometimes ritually "purified" before opening by the burning of  
sage, etc.  incense in chillout rooms.   distribution of oranges or other  
fruits.

Unfortunately, many have come to view drug taking, or better yet:=
 psychedelic journeying, as a fairly low-grade, low investment (not=
 fiscally speaking) recreational diversion. One should not, however,=
 forget that many of these substances do not simply enhance or distort=
 *reality*, but rather, open doors to entirely *different* dimensions.=
 The tools we're talking about here, especially psilocybin, DMT and=
 other derivatives of naturally occurring plant psychoactives, have=
 an aeon-old, and continuing tradition on this planet of being used=
 to do serious commerce with no less than *the gods*. =20

Let's imagine for a moment a dimension inhabited by no less than=
 the souls of all that have come before us and the all that may yet=
 come. A repository and domain of instantiation of all the psychic=
 energy in the universe. All the fairies, demons, pixies and prophets=
 that so colorfully adorn our history and mythologies. What if they're=
 all *real*. What if you don't need to meditate for twenty years=
 to get there. What if you don't have to be worthy. What if a simple=
 chemical like serotonin, or psilocybin (sp?) is all that it takes=
 to get there? What if that's why they're here...

These are journeys that should not be taken lightly. Indeed *fear*=
 may be the appropriate response. This does *not* however mean that=
 these journeys should not be taken, but rather, that they *be taken*=
 -- seriously.

Check out: "The Archaic Revival" & "Food of the Gods" both by Terrence=
 McKenna for more thoughts on the subject.

Mark asks what Jungle is:

I'm not exactly sure, but I'll tell you what I know.  Jungle is
a English and US East Coast thing, it's a form of  dance music that,
as well as I can describe from hearing a Jungle DJ from Philly
(Odyssey in case anyone cares) is a sort of melding of hard house
and break beat.  It's fast and energetic, and a bit dark and a bit
tribal.

If you really want the full scoop and a better definition write to
the ne-raves list becuase I know there are two people there (Joe
Le Sense and Damian Higgins) who are really into it and could give
a better definition and can list tracks that are good examples.

Laura

I am registering my extreme distress at the amount of open talk
about drugs on this list.  I do not feel comfortable with such
volume of this traffic coming into my accounts.  I do not wish to be 
identified by association with such activities as a result of me being
a member of the sfraves list.  I did not get into raving to do
drugs, and drugs are not why I still rave.  My primary interest
is the music (which rarely ever gets discussed here), followed by the 
friendships I have made as a result of going to parties and hanging 
out with list people.

Email I have received in response to my last letter has been
overwhelmingly in favor of continued detailed drug talk.  But
just because that is what the vocal majority wants it does not
mean I or the very few peole who wrote to me in agreement have to 
like it.  I have no authority over what goes on here, that ultimately 
lies with the person in the Stanford Medical School who graciously 
donated us the use of techno.stanford.edu to run the list on.  I am 
merely stating my level of distress and discomfort.

I know my options are to either stay on the list and ride it out
or get off the list, so you don't need to write me to tell me so.
I'll keep my nose out of this issue now that I've said my piece.

Laura

People: Time for a software solution, not a people solution - if you want
   to filter out email, it's pretty easy on most systems - just run a stupid
   filter which grep's for the words "drug" "cybin" etc. and autokills the
   mail.  They work great, and preserves freedom of speech for the rest of us.

Here's how to order: (Unix only, sorry- other ways on PCs and Macs, I'm sure)
1. make sure the program "slocal" is available - it's part of "mh", so take
   the man pages on mh ("man mh") and if it shows up, then it's installed.
2. create a file in your home directory called ".maildelivery"  In it, put
   stuff like:
---cut here---

# deletes all incoming mail with this subject
Subject "useless mail subject"	destroy	A	-

# deletes all mail with the word "drug" anywhere in it
*       drug    destroy  A  -

# deletes all mail from dickhead@cs.berkeley.edu
From    dickhead@cs.berkeley.edu    destroy A -

# you can match against any mail header field, like:
# To
# Subject
# Sender
# X-      <--- really useful for MIME and other wacky mail foo

# at the end put in this line, but replace /var/spool... with your mail
#   file.  To find it, run "env | grep MAIL".
default		-		>	A	/var/spool/mail/asah

---cut here---

3. create a ".forward" file, also in your home directory, with:
---cut here---
| /usr/lib/mh/slocal -user asah

---cut here---

You'll want to change that /usr/lib/mh/slocal path to the one on your
   system for running slocal.  Do a "which slocal" to find it.  Also,
   you'll want to change the -user flag, right...

Enjoy,
adam

ps. if you do this, experiment first... fooling around with email without
   testing your changes leads to lost mail and other hassles...
pps. there's a lot more cool stuff to slocal but mostly useful if you're 
   mh to read mail.
ppps. there are other ways to do this, but slocal is one of the best.
   Also, slocal and mh probably port to the PC and to the Mac... check out
   the ftp site world.std.com:/src/mail/mh-6.8.3  or run "archie mh" to
   find others, if archie's installed locally.

        Just to add my two pennies:

	No one is saying here that drugs aren't a part of the scene;
in fact they are a somewhat important part.  The topic itself is
fairly relevant, which is why I have a whole directory dedicated to
it on the archive site. 

	However, "the devil is in the details" - I've had it stated in
no unclear terms that if the list were ever portrayed as being
drug-focused or encouraging illegal actions, the graces of the Medical
School Informations and Systems Group at Stanford could be in
jeorpardy.  Stanford has seen at least one professor get into very hot
water because of their position on psychedelics, so the issue is a
little sensitive with them.  I can justify the archive section by
calling it a public service, since the majority of the information
there is on a self-help basis.  But posts over the mailing list
carry a heavier weight, and people advocating the use of a particular
dosage level can be potentially troublesome, perhaps even to the point 
of yanking us off the system.

	I should make clear one thing: 50% of the posts I saw I
considered perfectly acceptable.  They advocated caution, didn't
admit to personal use (these posts are archived, remember) and
referred people to better sources on the subject.  This should
be the model to follow.

	As soon as I get a home machine plugged into the net
(hopefully around this summer) with a good-sized pipe, I'll be moving
most of the sensitive stuff to that machine, and then we won't have to
worry about things like this.  But for now we exist through some
extraordinarily good graces, so let's not abuse it.  The nitrous
thread a while ago almost killed us, so I wouldn't be doing my job if
I wasn't trying to prevent a repeat of that.

	Thanks.

	Brian

p.s. - I might actually make it out this weekend!

>        ALL OF THIS INFORMATION IS MY ****OPINION***** ONLY!
>        IT IS NOT SCIENTIFIC FACT OR ANY OTHER FACT. USE AT YOUR
>        OWN RISK.

Not to be negative and argumentative (yeah, right), but I think your
opinions about drug use are a load of crap.  You shouldn't try to diagnose
and prescribe drugs to people you've never met in 5 paragraphs of sweeping
generalizations. 

>        Read Substance D by Phillip K Dick. the best book about drugs
>        I've ever read.

The book I think you're refering to is "A Scanner Darkly", which is PKD's
anti-drug book that he dedicated to several of his friends who he lost to
drugs.  The main characters in Dick's stories are often based on real people
from his life.  This main character is a drug dealer who sells "Substance D"
to his friends and housemates, and also works part time as a narc.  ("D"
stands for "Death".)  Things start getting weird when he's assigned to keep
an eye on himself (this is possible because the police department is so
infilterated that the narcs' identities must be protected by some interesting
technology that I won't go into. You'll have to read the book to find out
who's really behind the manufacture and distribution of Substance D).
This is definitly one of Dick's more psychotic stories, not his best, but
really up there.  (I had a hard time finding that book, but I was finally 
lucky enough to run across a first edition hardback copy that came from
a U.S. Air Force base library in Florida!)

        -Don the Dick Head

PS: I'm putting together an online World Wide Web hypermedia database and 
conspiracy graph of the works of Philip K Dick, so I would really appreciate
contributions of any interesting materials or immaterials about Philip K Dick!

PPS: Just like using certain drugs, some people just shouldn't read Philip K
Dick, since he can be MUCH more powerful than mere drugs.  But there's no way
to know if Dick is right for you, without trying it first.

I think the important thing to remember here is that
*everything* relating to drug use is like anything
else- subjective. What one person sees as a complex
soul searching experience could be another person's
light 'n easy good time.

anything- drugs, religion, a new house, look at what
you want out of it, think about whether your
expectations and goals are realistic, and *then*
decide. Don't do something like this for the wrong

InterNex Information Services is a growing Internet service provider
that specializes in helping businesses do business on the Internet.
We provide our customers "one stop shopping" for high-bandwidth
connectivity utilizing leading edge technology.  We also address the
need for Internet presence by providing electronic publishing services
such as WWW, Gopher, WAIS and FTP.



        SYSTEM and NETWORK MANAGEMENT ENGINEER

     InterNex is seeking a versatile and dynamic individual to be a
senior technical contributor in our rapidly growing Network Operations
Center.  This multifaceted job will involve all aspects of network and
system administration and management in a TCP/IP based, public
internet.  You will have a key role in the design and construction of a
wide area internet that incorporates high bandwidth technologies such as
ISDN, Frame Relay, T1, SMDS, and ATM.
     You will  participate in the design, construction, and maintenance
of a variety of network devices and software that generate and sustain
the growing area of Cyberspace for which InterNex is responsible.  You
will also support in-house development, including writing software to:
facilitate network management, perform connection billing,  implement
IP throttling, automate DNS configuration.
     You will also provide technical expertise to customers with
varying levels of technical sophistication and support other members
of the InterNex team.  You should  have good writing skills and be able
to communicate clearly.
     This job requires proven proficiency with C/C++ programming, Sun
System Administration skills, a solid working knowledge of the IP
protocol suite, router configuration, DNS configuration, and firewall
construction.  Experience with IPX, AppleTalk, IEE-802.x, SNMP, X.500,
ATM are pluses.  Knowledge of Telco systems, and project leadership
skills are desirable.  Commitment to teamwork is an essential aspect of
the job.  Educational requirements are MSEE/CS +2 years or BSEE/CS + 4
years or equivalent work experience.

     InterNex is located in the highly desirable mid-peninsula
community of Menlo Park.  Close to Stanford University, on the edge of
Silicon Valley, 35 minutes from the Pacific Ocean and San Francisco.
InterNex offers a high quality of life and a team of professionals
dedicated to setting new standards of excellence in technology and
customer service.

For immediate consideration, please e-mail your resume (no PostScript
or troff, please) to personnel@internex.net, or fax it to  (415)
473-3062. No phone calls please. InterNex is an equal opportunity

Subject: historical reference:  British rave organizers come to San Francisco

   But the music was unable to save the British rave scene, which collapsed  
under its own weight.  It had simply gotten too big, too commercial, too  
mainstream, therefore too un-hip, to keep the core ravers interested.  At its  
height, circa 1989, there were thousands of ravers, partying in the crop  
circles at 4 a.m., drinking juices and dosing up on XTC in London.  Three  
years later, it was over.
   Governmental pressure, says one ex-British raver, also contributed to the  
demise of the English rave scene.  The ravers, it seems, didn't fit in.  If  
they were outside in a field somewhere dosed up on smart drinks, they weren't  
hanging out at the corner pub, hoisting a pint of ale.  They were outsiders  
who were perceived as threatening.  According to 30-year-old Jas. Morgan, the  
music and arts editor of the cyberpunk bible _Mondo_2000_, the rave scene  
"caused economic grief with established organizations."  Enforcing a law that  
forbade large gatherings, Morgan says, "The British government acquired a  
helicopter expressly for the purpose of flying around and looking down on  
these illegal raves, and finally they succeeded in snuffing out the scene in  
Britain."
   Undaunted, the primary rave-scene movers, the organizers of the parties,  
began looking for other suitable climates to recapture the original spirit.   
They looked at San Francisco, New York, Los Angeles.  They chose The City --  
which, considering San Francisco's legendary hospitality to exiles,  
visionaries and serious partyers, should surprise no one.
   [...]
   In a peculiar mini-reprise of the British pop invasion of the early '60s,  
the English ravers hit The City in the winter of 1991.

--Cynthia Robins, "The Ecstatic Cybernetic Amino Acid Test," San Francisco  
Examiner Image Magazine, 16 February 1992, p 10.

Oh how I love the media and how it can sometimes state things as if they
were the facts.  Here's my $0.02

>At its
>height, circa 1989, there were thousands of ravers, partying in the crop
>circles at 4 a.m., drinking juices and dosing up on XTC in London.  Three
>years later, it was over.

It's height was much more at the end of '91 I would say when I remember the
parties getting waaay massive, very crowded, lots of really young kids
suddenly turning up in brand new clothes, the music suddenly getting
commercial (Smart E's, etc.) and the organizers & DJs picking up (after
they made lots of money) and taking off for places like SF.

I hate the dead/not dead argument but the scene is hardly "over" in
Britain.  Just because a scene goes underground does NOT make it "over."  I
was recently there and let me tell you that there are some wicked parties
happening that are better than ever before.  They're just not in the
public's eye like they used to be.  Most people retreated to new clubs that
were created and many others began to embody the spirit of "Do it Yourself"
and organize their own parties. If you ask me, going underground has been a
good thing.  Looks like that what's starting to happen here too.

>"The British government acquired a
>helicopter expressly for the purpose of flying around and looking down on
>these illegal raves, and finally they succeeded in snuffing out the scene in
>Britain."

Haha!  I remember being at a 3 day party on top of a huge hill in Lewes
(Sussex) in the summer of last year and on the second day, the cops made
their appearance with a helicoptor hovering overhead but they couldn't do
anything since the party was held on private property and we weren't
disturbing anyone  :)

>--Cynthia Robins, "The Ecstatic Cybernetic Amino Acid Test," San Francisco
>Examiner Image Magazine, 16 February 1992, p 10.

Yes, there is one that I have that one of the tracks was recorded live at
the Warfield in 1992. I went to that concert so I bought it as a memento.

London, UK SW11

The other CD was a companion to a video produced by Rose X Media House for 
City of Tribes Communications here in the City and is available through:

Astralwerks
114 West 26th Street
New York, NY 10001

If you want the video (which I have) it's $20 from

Backroads Music
418 Tamal Plaza
Corte Madera, CA
1-800-767-4748

Rox

From sfraves-owner  Mon Mar 28 13:41:37 1994
Received: by techno.Stanford.EDU (4.1/1.34)

Received: from lizard.srv.PacBell.COM by pbssi.srv.PacBell.COM (4.1/SMI-4.1)
	id AA07916; Mon, 28 Mar 94 13:41:27 PST
Date: Mon, 28 Mar 94 13:41:27 PST
From: lxfogel@srv.PacBell.COM (Lee Fogel)
Message-Id: <9403282141.AA07916@pbssi.srv.PacBell.COM>
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: FMM - The Legend Continues
Cc: jlf3@mofo.com
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU


We got to Bonny Doon in record time, 1hr 15min from SF, parking at 4:15am.
By the number of cars, it was obvious that this was big, the biggest FMM 
ever.  I scoped out the scene as we descended into the frenzy and by 
comparison to the now famous Halloween Full Moon Massive, I estimated a 
crowd size of at least 3,000.  

Garth was on as we set up camp and linked up with various friends and
friends of friends.  The Normals and Gil showed up with their tent and 
joined our contingent.  We also ran into Ovid, Seth, Geoff, Ravi, Scott
(Cloud Factory), Cap'n Crunch, and a few others who I'll probably remember
immediately after posting this.  As is typical of weekend FMM's, there was
a certain amount of people blowing hollaring, being drunk, shooting off 
fireworks, etc.  There seemed to be a lot less nitrous present, though.  
Janie & I just relaxed during this period, and things settled down into a 
pretty cohesive vibe just before dawn arrived.  Initially, I thought 
there was something wrong with the sound system cause there were so many
people crowding around the speakers that the sound was almost completely 
muffled.  This situation improved by the time Markie took the helm, 
somewhere around 6.   

I'm still struggling to find the words to describe Markie's set, which was
at least 4 hours long.  I've been a Markie admirer for a long time, and 
this was the best set I've *ever* heard him spin; acidic, trancy, funky - a 
totally incredible musical journey.  He never faltered and you could sense
his focus, like a wizard mesmerized by his own spell, yet still in command 
of it.  Around 9, the generator died for about 45 minutes, after which he 
came back to pick things up right where he left off.

This party pretty much proved to me that the scene still has a lot of
momentum in it.  There were a lot of new (to me, anyway) faces there, but
just about everyone seemed to know exactly what it was all about.  I wonder 
how many there were brought there by the April Rolling Stone article that
has now lifted the FMM  parties into official cult status.  There were 
certainly a few tourists in attendance, but I don't think that this 
detracted from things at all. 

By the time the generator came back on, the few hundred of us who remained 
were totally under the spell of things.  At this  point, I felt like I 
really was part of some of a quasi-religious cult: The shamen-DJs in 
conjunction with nature's energy and the altered states of consciousness of
the participants created a religious atmosphere - its vague dogma loosely
defined by the unspoken sharing of feelings and sensations.  It is 
fascinating to me how there can be so much understanding without words, 
where the experience that is taking place at that moment says it all.  
Bonnie Doon beach, surrounded by cliffs and the ocean provides a very 
spiritual setting for a rave.  But I have to wonder how much longer these 
parties are going to be allowed to continue there, now that the're getting 
so much attention.

When Jeno came on, the music jumped to an even higher energy level.  The
type of stuff he played in this a set is hard to describe.  It's kind of 
hardcore, but not in the high bpm or stripped down head pounding way.  The 
music is incredibly thick and tribal, an all out manic assault of 
multilayered sound timbres, music so rhythmic and intense that going along 
with it either requires that you already be tripping, or it makes you trip 
just as you allow your psyche to be absorbed by it.  I was pretty much 
blown away during this period, with my occasional attempts to rest 
consistantly curtailed by music that demanded my soul's participation.  I 
was able to come back into my surface-self when Jeno's set ended and Thomas 
came on with some horribly cheesy disco, as if to tell us, "I'm not Jeno 
so don't even expect anything like that from me."  Don't worry Thomas, I 
don't think we will ever get you two confused.

Thankfully, Thomas ceased torturing us, eventually veering off into some 
pleasantly funky grooves.  But we were totally spent and had already had
too much sun.  So at arounf 1:30 we packed things up, making sure to take 
our garbage with us.  I was bummed about forgetting to bring garbage bags 
to help with the overall cleanup - something I normally do at free outdoor 
parties.  Oh, well.  This party was a particularly messy one.

Back by the road there was an army of towtrucks and CHPs doing their
thing.  What a bummer it must of been for those who left the party
completely drained and still buzzing only to find their vehicle missing. 
I'm not even sure if there's a payphone within walking distance.

Although it is true that raving in the SF Bay area has to some extent lost 
the sense of excitement that comes with anything new and "on the edge", it 
is parties like the Full Moon Massive that will keep the scene alive here.  
Why?  Well, while most indoor raves now seem to be basically a very nice 
variation of the club scene,  FMMs remind us that the roots of raving are 
really intertwined with ageless tribal rituals of music, dance, trance, and 
the partaking of mind expanding sacraments, where reaching a oneness with 
our inner nature links us to a oneness with the forces of nature around us 
and in each other.  You don't have to watch many National Geographics to 
see the obvious similarities between parties such as these and the religious 
ceremonies of more "primitive" cultures.  Ritualistic raving will remain 
viable because it appeals to the sense of spirit in us that has been viable 
since the dawn of human consciousness.  I think the Wicked people who put 
on the FMMs understand this; that the scene is about much more than making 
money by helping people have fun.  It's about what it means to be alive in 
a way that goes beyond the artificial limits imposed by modern society.  On 
Sunday we were a tribe of the Universe, of the basic essence of life and 
energy, body and mind.  And in addition to all that, it was a fucking blast.
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
Lee Fogel/\/\/\/\/\eVerything/\Is/\possiBlE/\/\/\/\/\lxfogel@srv.pacbell.com
____________________________________________________________________________

Around midnight Saturday night a group of us met up with Ethan,
Bryce, and the pirate radio broadcaster for an evening of dancing
while broadcasting.  Unfortunately wind conditions prevented set-up
of the gear, so we headed to 24th street.

Rather than having to rent a van to haul the huge *SoundVision* system,
Johnny Turpin leant his speakers, and the whole set-up fit nicely
into the back of Ethan's jeep/vehicle.  

We got going around 1.30, and Lee An provided an interesting set 
ranging from that kind of house that includes divas singing up to
techno trance.  The highlight for me was when he played Fuse's
"Substance Abuse" which had me jumping and moving and sliding around
like my mind was connected to Richie Hawtin's LFO's.  I want that 
record :-).

I got to spin for a little while, and then Ethan had a turn.  Ethan
is really doing well, he puts together a totally different set every
time I hear him.  I really respect that in a DJ.  The high point of his
set was when he played some things off of the Orbital Peel Sessions.
Most of us were tired and had stopped dancing but when he got to that
track we all got an energy surge and then ended the evening on that
pleasant high note.

We packed up a bit after 4am, having enjoyed ourselves greatly.  A lot
of people have been saying that this Spring/Summer will be a good one.
Well, Ethan/Bryce/SoundVision/Liquid Air will be right in there
putting out good low-key parties all season long, if Saturday night's
brief but beautiful gathering is any indication.

Thanks guys, you made my Saturday!  I really needed it after eating
so much at Susie's mom's seder!

Laura

From: crunch@netcom.com (John Draper)

To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: Full moon madness
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Full Moon Madness in a MAJOR way
            By
       John T. Draper
        Cap'n Crunch
        
   Well,  after checking the location for "Generation" and learning that
the venue was 16th and Harrison (Goon city),   I decided at that point
to gear up and make plans for the Full Moon Rave (FMR) to take place
later that evening.   WOW!! A Full mooner on a Saturday night, Killer!.

   Already,  my phone was ringing off the hook as gobs of SFRavers, friends
and others were calling me for the location.   It was 10:30 PM at this point,
and I also called a few others to see if they got the location.    There
were several rumours floating around about the location being at Pt Reyes
but later on,  we dismissed it as rumours.

   The evening promised to be beautiful,   it was very clear,  although cool,
so rain wasn't going to be a problem.

   Amit,  one of my SFRaver freinds called me first to give out the location
which was near Bonny Doon.    Yukk!! we were hoping it would be north this time.

   Aaron and Matt had decided to abandon the idea of going because it was just
too far,  and Aaron had to work,  and Matt wanted to work on his house boat,
so I wound up going alone.   I called up Amit and agreed to meet at his place
in Mt View,  and we went together.   I arrive at Amit's place by 2:30 am,  and
we promptly leave for Santa Cruz.

   As we arrived at the site,  we see an endless line of cars estimated to be
about 3 miles long parked on the side of Hiway 1.    We parked and started the
2 mile hike,  looking for Panther beach (the allegid location).    As we were
waling along the Hiway,  we noticed people heading towards Bonny Doon and NOT
to Panther beach as was origionally planned and followed the crowd.    It
was reported that Panther Beach was just too small,  and with the tide coming
in,  we would have had LESS room,  so apparently it got moved up the road a
few miles.

   As we arrived,  we were stunned at how many people were already there,  and
so many campfires,  tents,  and other amenities.    The DJ stand was placed
against the cliffs this time,  aimed slightly out towards the ocean,  thus
made for a spacey echoing effect as the sounds bounced off the steep cliffs.
The music had started as we arrived (approx 3:15 am),  but the music wasn't
that loud (At least not from up on the cliffs).   As we approached,   the
huge crowds became more evident as we made our way near the speakers,  and
explained the reason why we couldn't hear the music that well.

   The crowd was densly packed near the two speakers,   and had problems finding
a clear dancing spot.   But the music was incredable.    I actually heard some
new stuff,  cleverly put together by Markie Mark as I heard one of his best sets
ever.     

   My knee,  now almost totally healed,  allowed me to dance continiously from
3 am to 3 pm,  resting only a few times.    This was the first time that everything
in my body is totally healed,  and not even my cronic back problem came
into my conciousness.   My brain was in a very high state of "tweakeyness",  and
got so totally absorbed in the music,  inventing new dance movements I never
tried before,  although quite sucessfully.   I was getting off in a major way,
under the cloudy skies,  so never actually saw the moon (Except while going 
over the mountains on the way to the beach).   The moon was far from my mind
it it's altered state,  as the music was my heartbeat and source for energy
that never stopped until the generator died around 9 am.    It turned out
that everyone was so absorbed by the parying that nobody even thought that
the generator needed gas.    Once it stopped,   at first everything was in
total stillness.    There was little talking,  and people were very dazed out.
There was little or no interactions going on,  people just stood and stared around
wondering if it got busted.  

   I wandered near the generator to see what had happened and learned that
some bozo put water in the tank instead of gasoline.  Ooops!!   so for about
45 minutes as some mechanical types volunteered to flush out the water,  others
went out for more gasoline,  and eventually the generator choked back to life.

   Markie was still on at that time,   but cued up a really slow trancey song
with NO BEAT to gradually get the crowd used to the fact that the DJ'ing was
to start soon.    By this time,   I would estimate about a third of the crowd
had left.   Eventually Markie's song transmuted into the familiar boom boom beats
and I was right there.   Actually,  I had already started dancing (even to the
trancey stuff,  experimenting with a slow thai chi type dance movements,  getting
my body warmed up again).   When the first beats started pumping out,  I was
ready and raring to go.

   My estimation is about 2500 crazy raver folks out there "getting down" to the
serious business of raving and partying.    After the 45 minute generator problem,
I had NO PROBLEM finding a killer spot near the speakers and I don't think I
stopped dancing until about noon.    After Markie,  Jeno spun and incredible
set.   I don't think I stopped dancing (Except for an ocassional stretch) all
throughout his very long 2 hour set.   Jeno took me on one of the tranciest
rides I've been on for a very long time,  yet his sets had a pretty good amount
of variaty.   Best I heard from Markie and Jeno for a very long time,  and both
played a lot of new stuff.

   By about 1 pm I was getting stronger and stronger,  my body wasn't complaining
at all.     But with me,   I always seem to get into better and stronger dance
style towards the end.    It was also nice not to have to stop at 7 am (At end
of indoor rave) and go to some "Afterparty".    It was a very good continious
12 hours of non-stop dancing,  the kind that I prefer,  although last summer,
when at LoveStock,   it was 24 hours of continious dancing ( I kike THAT much
better).

   Thomas took to the turntables after Jeno,   and his start was kinda slow,  and
Disco like,  so I took the opportunity for my first good stretch break since about
6 am.    After that, schmoosed a while with friends,  and by that time,  Thomas
was into some pretty good stuff,   so I headed out there till the very last note.
Sometime during his set,  he made an announcement that cars were getting towed
away,  so I go look for Amit to make sure he checkes his car.

   I danced Thomas's set to the very end,  when he put on this very slow tune,
and I stopped my highly energetic style,  slowed down to some great stretchey
moves to iron out a few kinks.    Thomas's last tune (Kinda housey) gave me
another spurt of energy to round out one of the best Full Mooner's I've been
to in a long time.   And I was begiining to think the scene has died,   Boy!!
Was I Wrong!   The SF Scene here is even richer than ever....   And I get rumours
that BOOGIE BUFFET is coming back!!   This upcomong Thursday,  the Sisters will
be back again... Oh!!  Goodie,  I can hardly wait....  I sure miss them...

Cheers
Keep the scene alive
Cap'n Crunch

From sfraves-owner  Tue Mar 29 00:37:19 1994
