From: Seth Joshua Horvitz <acid23@uclink.berkeley.edu>
Subject: FMM, Morris on KALX, etc...
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Message-Id: <Pine.3.89.9403282352.A2897-0100000@uclink.berkeley.edu>
Mime-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; charset=US-ASCII
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU


Just to balance out the long and beautiful posts by Lee and the Cap'n, 
here are some of my negative observations of this weekend's FMM:

Music: As a whole, I'd have to say I was pretty disappointed.  Every time 
I heard a song that I liked, I would get up and dance, only to be sent 
back to the blanket two songs later with another boring 
BOOM-CHIC-BOOM-CHIC, 1-2-3-4 boring house track.  Now don't get me wrong, 
I can get into house, but if I'm going to really trance out, I need 
acid.  This DOESN'T mean 303's necessarily; in fact, acid can 
mean almost anything, whether it's a crazy freaked out funky beat, a 
bubbling synth, or a tweaky sample.  There just has to be something in 
the music that gives my mind a challenge.  Most of the music at the FMM made 
me feel like my intelligence was being insulted.  There were too many 
breaks designed purely to make hundreds of people on E scream and whistle 
and go crazy.  A really good break SHOULD make you scream and go crazy, 
but it shouldn't require "enhancement" for its effects.  To me, a bad 
house song is like a bad movie; if you know exactly what's going to 
happen at every stage, it isn't enjoyable.

I agree that Markie was the main attraction (although I think I fell 
asleep during Jeno's set).  I was extremely impressed with his technical 
ability, always twiddling knobs, bouncing things from left to right.  The 
music was a bit choppy, although there were definitely brilliant tracks 
scattered throughout.  I was very pleasantly surprised to hear about 8 
minutes of  Plastikman's (Richie Hawtin) Electrostatik, an extremely 
minimal, but very trance-inducing acid track.  I was thinking about 
JSL's posts about Markie being the king of "trip-hop", but after 
hearing him, I'd have to say that the term seems much more 
appropriate in describing a DJ like Spun.  What do other's think? Overall, 
Markie's set was very enjoyable, but unfortunately, it often lapsed into the 
1-2-3-4 
house beats that I just can't get into.  Oh well, I guess this is what the San 
Francisco scene is known for, right?    

Well, those are really my only gripes.  I still had a good time, 
expecially since it was my first visit to Bonny Doon.  It was amazing to 
sit at the top of the hill and watch the movement patterns of thousands 
of people dancing, walking, congregating and hovering around fires.  From 
a distance, they all look like one unit, oozing around like that "Life" 
computer simulation (the one with all the little dots interacting).  

On the way home, at around 3, I realized that my face been slowly 
sizzling, and is now an uncomfortable shade of red.  I made it back just 
in time for my radio show, and I MEAN just in time.  After getting 
dropped off in front of Ameba, I ran to the Muni stop, transferred to 
Bart, ran home to pick up a few records and my headphones, and biked up 
to the station, arriving at 6:24, one night behind on sleep, for my show at 
6:30.  Phew!!

A few minutes later, I found out that KALX dj Minor had arranged to bring 
Mixmaster Morris in to do a guest set.  What perfect timing!  He arrived 
just before 8pm, and took over for the rest of the show with a sick 
blend of soft tweaky acid and ambient.  I kind of expected more from the 
non-techno realm (obscure classical and new-age, maybe), but he still 
managed to pull off a great hour-long set, with a little mini-interview 
in between.  

After the show, we took Morris down the street to Rasputin's, where he 
went utterly MAD (say with British accent), flipping through racks and 
racks of records and CD's at lighting speed,  from practically every 
section in the store.  The weird thing was, he could see every single 
record that flipped by, pulling things out all over the place to add to his 
stack.  As closing time neared, he was forced to weed down his collection to 
just two bags full (ouch!).  It was a hectic, though quite fun, 
experience :) 

I didn't make it to Ambience, since I am not 21, but I haven't seen 
any reviews yet.  What did people think?

my weekend in a nutshell...
//////////{{{{{{{{{{(((((((((([[[[[[[232]]]]]]]]))))))))}}}}}}}}}\\\\\\\\\\\
-Seth

From sfraves-owner  Tue Mar 29 05:06:38 1994

From sfraves-owner  Tue Mar 29 12:10:55 1994
Received: by techno.Stanford.EDU (4.1/1.34)
	id AA18990; Tue, 29 Mar 94 12:10:55 PST
Received: from soda.berkeley.edu by techno.Stanford.EDU (4.1/1.34)
	id AA18983; Tue, 29 Mar 94 12:10:47 PST
Received: (laura@localhost) by soda.berkeley.edu (8.6.8/PHILMAIL-1.10) id MAA29396 for sfraves@techno.stanford.edu; Tue, 29 Mar 1994 12:10:44 -0800
Message-Id: <199403292010.MAA29396@soda.berkeley.edu>
From: laura@soda.berkeley.edu (Laura La Gassa)
Date: Tue, 29 Mar 1994 12:10:42 -0800
X-Mailer: Mail User's Shell (7.2.3 5/22/91)
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: The Eighth House
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Well, I think the moon was still in the 7th House last night or something
because the 8th House, while a good idea, suffered in its execution.

I was told it started at 9 so I said I'd be there at around 8.30 to
check out the mixer and so Brian could set up his DAT tape.  I arrived
with Brian, Tamara, Bryan, Dana, and Andy, only to find that nothing was 
even remotely ready to go.  The manager of the club didn't arrive until 7.15
to let the 8th House crew in to decorate and set up, so they were very
behind schedule.

The place was decorated nicely, with very odd giant-sized dayglo mystical
3-d symbols hanging over the dance floor, and large posters with the
name of the DJ by the booths so you'd know who was spinning when.
There were lots of small candles around, too.  However, a club is a club
and to me you just can't decorate away the looming fact of multiple huge
bars and signs put up by the management that say things like "New dress
code -- no hats, no t-shirts" which we blatantly ignored anyway.

The club was the Oasis down at 11th and Folsom.  They set up the ambient
DJs in the Egyptian lounge room and the trance DJs on the main floor.
The first ambient DJ was K.S.P. and his idea of ambient included hours
of grating discordant noises and sounds that reminded us of cows being
slaughtered.  It was not pretty.  Mind-crunching ambient in doses at
the right times is great, but it went on and on and on and on and on . . .
Mixmaster Morris arrived much later (around midnight), but I missed
him because I was on in the main room.

Ahh, the main room.  What a complete waste of stereo equipment.  The
volume wasn't loud enough (if you are in the booth with the monitor on
and you can still hear people down on the floor talking it is clearly
not loud enough), the bass was all distorted, there was no mid-range, and
all the trebel seemed to be in the bar area.  People came into the booth
all night asking us to turn it up or fix it but we couldn't because the
owner had the keys to the case where the main amps were and he spent 
much of the night in his office or on the phone basically ignoring us.
I was dying for Ethan and Bryce to swoop down and magically fix things,
but of course they couldn't because it wasn't their stuff (and Ethan
wasn't there, but it's a good thing he wasn't or he would have cried
over the sound).

Things finally got started a bit before 11 (this was supposed to open at 9),
and Sir Sensual came on in the main room.  He had the nicest most joyous
trancey records, and he also brought along a small Prophet synth that he
programmed and ran patterns and played over some of his records.  No one
wanted to take over from him because the sound was so bad, but at midnight
I went up and had my turn.  During my set Mixmaster Morris's manager Russell
came up to say  hi and thank me for playing "Gravitational Arch of 10" which
is one of his favorite tracks, and he also asked me if I could do anything
about the sound.  Just as I said "no, I can't, and it totally sucks" the
club's alleged sound guy FINALLY arrived.  He was rather pissed at my
outspoken evaluation, but it was true.  He said "What do you mean this
sucks?  This is my gear and it's fine."  Well, he must be deaf from too
many years of Metallica or Danzig at high volumes, because it really was
bad.  He then proceded to get in my way and fiddle with the mixer and stuff
trying to fix things.  At last he got the heck out and I continued on for 
a total of 45 minutes.  

I turned the tables over to D.M.A. who had some beautiful records but seemed 
so annoyed with the sound man and the bad sound (even after the sound guy 
supposedly adjusted things) that he didn't bother to even try to mix properly.  
Jonah was sitting up there in the booth with us going "This totally sucks, why 
are we even here?  What is the point of playing if it is going to sound so 
bad."  Russell later introduced me to Morris saying "poor girl, she did a good 
job of fighting it out with the sound system in the other room."  

The absolute worst happened during D.M.A.'s set:  the sound guy claimed the
bad sounds were the problem of the cartridge and stylus on the turntables.  He 
replaced one table's standard Techniques set-up with an Ortofon, but guess 
what, it didn't help the fact that the rest of the system was EQ-d wrong!  Even 
worse, he removed the other table's headshell and WALKED OFF WITH IT.  So when 
D.M.A.'s record ran out he was screwed!  The music stoped for a second and 
D.M.A. just let the next track on the record play because there was nothing to 
mix to.  

Well, I've bitched enough, you get the picture.  Bad sound kills a party
before it can even begin.  Good sound is even more important than stellar
DJs and good drugs.  Without good sound a party is NOTHING.  Philip,
the 8th House organizer, asked me if I'd come back and spin again in
two weeks, and I said I would but only if they fixed the sound system.
So we'll see.

So anyway, while the trance DJs were fighting with the sound in the main 
room, Morris had to contend with the "Hyper*Sentient" dancers in the
ambient lounge.  Apparently they did this 5 minute or so "interpretive
dance" that involved body paint, grimacing, and dancing in and around
large cardboard boxes.  Brian can give a much more detailed description.
He says that Morris looked out at them at one point with a "what the HECK?"
expression on his face :-).

The crowd there was interesting:  a good number of net-ravers and friends
of net-ravers (it seems that if you have a sfraves DJ at a small party
it guarantees that at least a dozen net-people will show up, plus assorted
non-net friends) plus confused people who used to come to the Oasis when
it was the Temple of Psychik Youth night (or whatever).  What was very
interesting is that the music did reach both the TOPY group and the 
raver group.  It was good to look down and see guys in black with 
leather, studs, chains, and interesting alchemical signs getting as
deeply into the music as longtime ravers like Brian Sassonne and Marlo.
The support from the sfravers was great to have!  Thanks for coming!  
I think that if only the sound system had been halfway decent more people
would have been drawn into the trance web we were attempting to weave.

I left about 1.30 in the morning, and Morris was still spinning.  According
to Philip the party was to end at 2am.  Overall I'd say that The 8th House
was a very GOOD idea and that Philip and his group did a good a job as
they could putting it on.  The sound system, the setting, and it being
Monday night dampened things a lot.  If the sound system gets cleaned up
(doubtful) or if Philip finds another location it could be something REALLY
neat:  an intense 10-2 dose of trance to start your week off great.

See you,

Laura

Hear hear. I went to about 15 parties before I went to one with

system SUCKS and what the crowd hears isn't the THING that tweaked you
into the next dimension, but an earthquake.

It makes one really appreciate the sound people who work hard and get
it right.

>From pashdown@xmission.com  Mon Mar 28 14:01:33 1994
From: pashdown@xmission.com (Pete Ashdown)
Message-Id: <9403282201.AA22140@xmission.com>
Subject: Mixmaster Morris/Pete Namlook SF
To: idm@techno.Stanford.EDU (Intelligent Dance Music)
Date: Mon, 28 Mar 1994 15:01:08 -0700 (MST)
Cc: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU (SF Raves)

"Something different" was the general consensus on what people were expecting
from the completely ambient show with Mixmaster Morris, Pete Namlook, and
Spacetime Continuum.  There seemed to be a large excitement over the night
since for a large part the rave scene has run its course in breaking new
boundries.  In usual form, I'd flown into San Francisco for the weekend to
witness yet another event.

It was broadly advertised that there would be little to no dancing at this
show.  Pillows, beanbags, blankets and whatever were encouraged accessories.
The organizers had covered the dancefloor with a large padded carpet, then put
remnants around the top level balcony.  The decorations were definitely
homespun, but interesting nonetheless.  For the most part, the room looked
like a large psychedelic Arabian tent.  The sound itself was not obnoxiously
loud, just loud enough.  I sat near the speakers when it started with no
problems, but stuffed my ears with toilet paper later.  As I moved around the
room, I would take it out to hear better based on my placement.

Initially, I sat watching Spacetime Continuum do his stuff.  Although his
collaboration with Terrence McKenna makes me green, I do enjoy his solo music
quite a bit.  He concocted an interesting, yet varied set.  His show dipped
into dance, but not for long.  It seemed that whenever a beat kicked in, the
crowd cheered and started to throb.  Otherwise, the audience looked very much
like a large slumber party.

When Mixmaster Morris finally came on, he crouched in front of the carpet
behind two 1200's and a Denon 2000 (yay!!).  The beginning of his set started
with an old recording of relaxation techniques that was used on "Flying High"
as well.  Over the course of the night, he brewed a mostly beatless set.  I
only recognized a few tracks, and in his first set, there was no Irresistible
Force that I could place.  The reason I say this is because there were a
couple of tracks that sounded dead-on in the IF style.  Maybe we have another
album to look forward to in the near future?

While Morris was spinning, Pete Namlook sat behind him messing with some
equipment on the desk.  It was a subject for debate as to whether he was
actually doing anything or not.  What I believe it ended up being was the fact
that he was doing setup for his performance.  When Morris finished, Namlook
took over immediately with some light airy ambience that ranged from simple
sweeps into odd electronic noise.  About half an hour into this, THE BEAT
KICKED IN.  The largest cheer from the audience yet went up as this very slick
n' cool 110 bpm crusher bounced around the room.  Namlook let it fly for a
while, then when back to straight ambience.  This went on for a performance of
almost 90 minutes.  Frankly I wouldn't be surprised if the whole thing was
sent to DAT for later publishing.

Morris came back on and proceeded to mix into the morning.  This set was
airier, more angelic than the first.  I fell asleep twice, waking up to what
seemed like the heavens opening up for me.  Around 5:00 AM, the ambient
version of "Space is the Place" came on.  I smiled as he worked in Psychick
Warriors of Gaia's "Obsidian" underneath it.  I really think it was the best
thing he played all night.  What a brilliant track.  My only complaint with
his performance is that it wasn't much of a performance.  I would have much
rather seen him do something live and/or play more of his own material.  This
is why I feel Namlook bested him.

Overall an excellent show.  Certainly nothing like the Orb or Orbital shows I
was in town for previously, but a certain newness prevailed.  Besides the fact
that this was an over-21 show, I think there was an even older crowd present.
It seems that whenever a new idea comes around the highschool kids are the
last to embrace it.  The ambient slumber party may or may not take off as a
replacement for rave, but I certainly think it has some potential.  I received
one flyer from a DJ who I had seen do ambient rooms at Wicked events
advertising an ambient outdoor event.  If it wasn't so cold here right now,
I'd fire up the generator and do one of my own.  Instead, all I have to do is
look forward to summer.

Hello there all.  This is another view of the weekend.  I think I am the
only person that attended both Liquid Air and the Full Moon so I have some
comparing to do between big and small.  First off I went to Carmen's
birthday party at JMAR's house where I met Bryce, JMAR and the
aforementioned Carmen.  Alas my car was broken into but not much of a
trouble to me (they didn't steal my new records out of the front seat what
a godsend).  Then I headed over to Jon Drukman's house where I met numerous
sfravers.  We chilled and chatted and had little bits of food.  Thanks to
Jon and John for both opening up there houses to the list and being very
gracious hosts.  I then drove Susie over to Brian and Laura's place and we
prepared for Liquid Air gathering some warm clothing.  We proceeded to Twin
Peaks and were greeted by really strong winds and beautiful smiling faces.
We headed over to a place near the waterfront in the wherehouse district
and set up a few feet from the ocean.  At most I think there were 15 people
there but the vibe and the people were the best I've been around in a
looooonnnnngg time.  I grooved until about three there and reluctantly
drove down to Santa Cruz on my way home.  I stopped at the Full moon about
half a mile away actually.  It was way to big if you ask me.  One of my
friends that I ran into almost was picked a fight with and I heard a couple
of the "Watch out!" kind of unfriendly comments when I accidentally ran
into people dancing.  When I left some of the cars had been flyered with
these big ugly (imho) snoop.e flyers.  I think it's great to see our scene
growing but not at the cost of sacrificing the unity and family like
felling that were being fostered when I left last September.  I hope  I'm
not seeing another demise cycle in the scene.  The flyer I picked up looked
like cheese all over with little e-inuendos all over it which I had thought
people got over.  Not as much nitrous as Lee noted but a friend of mine
noted that there was lots of speed=bad (imho) which can create more
beligerrence and blah,blah, blah...I also hope the beach was cleaned up
afterwards because it was trashed when I was there.  Sorry so negative but
I just don't want to see the scene explode again into what happened when it
exploded in the summer of '92.  The newness may be gone for you but let the
newness go away for others, remember the feeling you had when you were at
your first rave?  if it was good do you still think people are getting that
attention, loving, and friendliness that I got and hopefully you got? just
pondering some more...we could do so much more with lots of smaller
parties...even on the same night...

The Cloud Factory
Our People Make the Difference

From sfraves-owner  Tue Mar 29 22:09:11 1994

    i attended the Ambience thing saturday, i really enjoyed it.  the only 
thing i didn't enjoy was the price ($15) cuz i hadta leave a little after
3am - girlfriend couldn't fall asleep due to no pillows - next time remember
to bring pillows and blankets to ambient events.
    the music from 11pm to 2:30 was spacey and cerebral - really got my
imagination going.  at times i really felt like i was tripping.  didn't have
to use ear plugs until around 3 when some really brain penetrating sub bass
things were going off - cleans out the mental cobwebs.  i especially liked
the tweeks, blurps, and churps - made a laugh out load a couple times.
    the visuals were entertaining.  film loops of cosmos, space ships,
animated robots, flowers, fractals, and mandalas.  for the most part the visuals
enhanced the music - effective trip matching.
    mellow crowd, not alot of cig. smoking, some herb was around, and you know
king st. serves alcohol, so a lot of people were drinking.  and a lot were
flat out asleep.  i guess $15 bucks is cheaper than a hotel.  seems there was
a lot of people getting in for free on guest list.  but the place was pretty
packed.  bean baged souls on a sea of ambient tranquility.

barry

howdy all,

it has been forever since i've posted, but i had a really good weekend
anad thought that i would tell the tale.

in the condensed format:

Friday night i was going to go to Saturday Night Fever at the roxie as a
weird thing to do with a bunch of friends.  we were not the only ones
with this idea, sold out.  so we went to the elbo room and waited for
the sprial jive line to post the local of the party.  wait awile and
finally got it.  gathered up blankets and sweaters, we were off.  after
we arrived directions were given to us by a guy who hide in a bush.  we
fucked up those directions and proceded to have quite an adventure tring
to find the space.  when we got there there were only about 10 people.
We made a camp of blankets and got settled and took turns wandering and
exploring.  music was good to great all night.  sound system was great,
anyone know whose it was?  we left about 5am.

Sat: my girlfriend and i went to 20 tank waiting for the ska show at
slims to open up.  hi-top beer there is really good but they are not
fucking kinding about it packing a wallop.  after drinking for a couple
of hours we went to slims and checked out a couple of the bands.  we
were planing to go to the B-day party later but this was preemtived my
my girlfriend drinking too much.  thus the night was short on going out
but adventursome.  (note: a really nice homeless man helped me out in
taking care of my friend,  he also didn't ask for anything in return, i
palmed him a 10 spot and thanked him,  it always improves my day and all
to meet geniunly nice people. (especially since my car was broken into
earlier that night)).  

sunday:  went roller-blading for my first time, yet another adventure.
also watched a bunch of people in KMEL shirts around an incredably poor
sound system for the dancing section of the closed road.  reminds my of
the sunday in the park  (permits?)

Monday:  back to school, then drove 4 hours back to SF for a private
party that my friend was throwing.  there i spun for about 2 hours, had
a great time.

ive got other news to post later this week

C-ya

that last one went out because leader dots + line wrap = UEOM
(Unexpected End of Message).  Repeat: "it's not a bug, it's a feature"
until you believe it :)

After spending quite a few weekends in San Francisco the last few months
it's been interesting having a more extended stay at home here in the
Northwest.  

Things started out on Friday, March 11 with the return of the Choclit
Factory gang, led by Tigger & Dred-Eye, in a fine event called 
Unity & Transcendance.  It was held at the Seamans' Union of the Pacific
hall on 1st Ave. in the Belltown district of Seattle.  A big concrete
room that was covered with chalk dust from the ceiling by the time we
were done in the morning!  After the tragic shooting outside the Velvet
Elvis in February it was very important for this event to work out well
and it did indeed.  A really good crowd, great DJs including Riz, Masa,
and others, finishing with an astonishingly good trance set by Nathan
which is already in the running for "Set of the Year" honors (four made
it on my list last year, so this is saying something!).  I got to play
around with Tigger's FractInt projection setup, which was jolly fun.

We rented a van and drove back to Portland for UHF's Leprechaunland
on Saturday night the 12th.  This was held in a fresh warehouse right
around the corner from the White Eagle Tavern (for those who know the
area).  Headlining back to back with long sets were Markie and Derrick
Carter, both on three 'tables.  It would have been a better vibe except
for the fact that the sound was excruciatingly loud in the mid-low-bass,
almost painfully so.  The dance floor was sparse all evening as a result.
I gave up and walked back downtown around 6 am through the deserted
Coliseum parking lot.  The new Trail Blazer arena is rising quickly . . .
someday we'll put a REAL show in there!

The following weekend, back to Seattle for another in the series of
Evolution parties, held just a few blocks south of the Kingdome in a
cozy warehouse space.  A little too cozy in a way, the place got very
hot and the floor was sopping wet from condensation.  But the party
got off really well.  Barry Weaver and Ernie Munson cranked it up, but then
Dub Tribe just knocked everyone's sox off with a set that transcended
their phenomenal Together birthday party set of a few weeks ago, if
that even seems possible.  Donald finished us off with some excellent
phat Deeetroit techno, the REAL stuff.  The space could have been better
but given the neurotic vibe that's been present at some of the other
Seattle parties I've been to this was a very good time overall.
We then dropped in to the after-party at the Velvet Elvis, which went
until at least 2 pm.  Some of the crew went off to a barn party somewhere
out Snohomish way but I bailed to catch the train back to Puddletown
at 5 pm.  

This past weekend was Portland's turn.  Friday night turned out to be
one of our better gatherings ever, even though it was at the old Greyhound
station, site of some of the weakest parties and worst sound I've ever
been unfortunate enough to experience.

However, this night turned that around, at least for once.  Sasha, Kimball
and John Digweed breezed through really fine UK-house-trance sets right
up me own alley.  JD's records were lost by the airline but found in time
for a late set.  But Sasha stole the show with an excellent set, mostly
*not* of his own stuff, played with panache and an exquisite sense of
timing.  The local DJs were all suitably impressed :)

The following night was a small party called 'Together' in an art gallery
over on the inner east side.  Actually it's quite a good location for
a smaller gathering, with two good sized rooms upstairs off the street
and no neighbors to complain about noise.  I don't know who all the DJs
were but Mike Stevens put in a fine set.  Brad Vachal had forgotten the
closing time for a downtown garage and his car (and records!) were locked
inside over night, so he had to use his non-standard stuff, didn't feel
that great about how things were going, and bailed off the 'tables early.
But I ended up chatting with him for a quite a while.  I really got a
sense of Portland starting to coalesce again as a scene with a distinct
personality instead of just a random collection of clubbers dressing down
'to rave', which is how it appeared to me a year ago.  there's been a
core all along which has been trying to put on good events and catch a
fire, but it's slow going.  The opening of Platinum Records (where Brad
is one of the main buyers) has really made a difference here - it's
a real DJ-oriented store and has helped provide an anchor for the scene.
At least it has for me!

The number of parties here in Portland is on the upswing again.  We have
Jeno coming in a couple of weeks, plus a bunch of other things.  Every
spring hope arises that Portland will finally get its act together, we
have all the right ingredients here.  Tune in again, same bat-time,
same bat-channel :)

I've been droppin' the phat beats in the comfort of my office.  I can't
compete with Eli's across the street or the Greek restaurant downstairs
when they play bouzouki (and especially when they smash the plates!),
but the booming sound in Oregon Pacific 305 is my new/old 1975 Yamaha
amp driving four satellites and a subwoofer.  Manoj of CORE was here
the other day and I regaled him with sounds from across the spectrum.
And I'm actually getting to the point where I can do a passable beat-
match a fair percentage of the time!  

Geoff White is in Seattle this week and I'm hoping for more cross-
fertilization between the Northwest and Bay Area this year.  Let's talk
about doing something around the Grateful Dead shows in Seattle and
Eugene in June, and keep yer earballs peeled for info about something
happening near the Country Fair in July.  And this is the time to start
thinking about *my* favorite idea, which is an all-weekend-long net.affair
outside somewhere with 36+ hours of music and a relaxing good time for all.

See you in . . . the future!

phred

Hey there, all!

Friday- I went with a friend to the new billiards hall in
downtown SJ. It was very expensive, but I guess we couldn't be
too surprised at that- it took us nearly an hour just to clear
one table. Towards the end of the game, we decided we were 
playing just to hear the sound of one ball hitting another ;)
ahhh, sweet music! Then we went to The Red Light District to
hear Grotus (add as many umlauts as you can); this band is best 
described as melody through percussion- lotsa noise!

Saturday I went to a birthday dinner for my daddy; that's it.

Sunday is pretty much negligable as far as house events go (except 
for my own personal house-cleaning stuff, but who wants to hear 
the details about taking water spots off of a mirror), 
but then comes Monday!

On Monday night I went to the second-ever meeting of a 
newly founded SJ women's collective. Although its constituents 
are primarily from the SJ house scene, we hope to include 
all kinds of different women. Basically, the group is going 
to be whatever we make of it and will include any activities that 
spark interest: from reading recommended books/articles and later
discussing them to volunteering for rape crisis centers and/or 
women's shelters, from participating in demonstrations and AIDS walks 
together to holding parties, from group camping to publishing a 
group newsletter for public distribution to  whatever else
interests the individual(s) of the group. If you hadn't 
guessed, there's no hierarchical structure to the group-
those women who want to participate can. 

Best surprise of the evening: I finally met Vivian and 
Lavonne (Hiya!)

The brainpower and spirituality of this meeting was so intense 
that I almost felt too wired to go to FreeLife, but I went anyway...
the energy was pretty diffuse- patches here and there. The set 
(who was playing when???? 12-2?) was a little too cowboy disco 
for my tastes- kinda reminded me of the roller rinks I used to 
frequent when I was seven, but it was fun to say hellos 
and do a little jig. I left early (1:30), dropped a friend by 
her house and went on my merry way to sleep, or to try to sleep 
anyway, as my head was still reeling from the meeting.

If any of you want more information about the group; meeting 
times, "all genders welcome" nights, etc..., just gimme an 
e-mail holler!

Jocelyn

Phred says:

>And this is the time to start
>thinking about *my* favorite idea, which is an all-weekend-long net.affair
>outside somewhere with 36+ hours of music and a relaxing good time for all.
>See you in . . . the future!

Yay!   I can hardly wait...  It's a long time since I was able to really
GET DOWN and boogie an entire weekend.    I hope I can get my car fixed soon
so I can start traveling around,  scouting for sites.

Say!  I got this killer idea,    Lets get together a small group of people
some weekend,  and go out driving around,   looking for suitable sites
to have killer outdoor gigs.   We could make a picnic/camping trip out
of it,   discover neat areas seldom visited by people.   Sorta like the
"Bay Area Backroads" places.     I remember a long time ago,  when I was
tinkering with the phone system,   I would go to some of the strangest
remotest places and hack their phone system.    All it takes is a good
map of California and the intention of having a good time exploring new
and strange places.     While I was visiting these places,  I would hang
out in the local gathering spots (pool halls,  etc),  and get to know the
locals.    That way, I was able to learn a lot about what goes on locally,
and I think that once we put forth the idea of having a rave/party in
their area,  they (The locals) would be more than willing to help us
get in contact with some of their friends who might have lots of private
land to have such a gig.    Most of the time,  at least in the summer,
these local folks living in remote areas would be really open to the idea
of having a real rave in their area.    It's worth checking out...

On the way up to Harbin Hot springs last summer,   I discovered an old 
race track out somewhere between San Rafael and Vallejo area (The Hiway
connecting the who cities),   and it appears to be far enough away from
homes.    I'll try and remember exactly where it is.   It was just as big,
if not bigger than the Livermore race track area where the Gathering was
held near the 4th of July (Remember the hill fire?).

Anyone else,  who goes driving around N. Calif should also keep a keen eye
out for such sites.    I think that it might be possible to locate the owners
of these places and negotiate a deal with them.   Of course we want the party
to be big enough to be fun,  but not super mega-large as to cause problems
in clean-up,  or other problems.    But predicting the size of such partys
is next to impossible.

Cap'n Crunch

Subject: A few words on Brian's Birthday
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

To: vrave@gnu.ai.mit.edu
Subject: a few moments of reflection

Today is Brian Behlendorf's birthday, and in honor of this I'm going
to say many words about this wonderful person.  Of course, you could
say I'm biased since he's my boyfriend, but if you look at the facts
of what he has accomplished you'll want to run up to him and give him
birthday hugs too.

The net-rave scene as we know it was started by Brian.  He started
raving in LA when acid house and Baby Ford were king.  When he moved
to Berkeley for college, he found out about the Internet and started
reading newsgroups, including alt.rave.  He then got the brilliant idea
to start a mailing list for ravers in the San Francisco area, and
sfraves was born in early March, 1992.  People from all over the US
subscribed, and sfraves spawned the rest of the lists that make up 
the net-rave scene today:  midwest, southeast, DC, northeast, mountain,
northwest, southern california, pittsburg-cleveland, and so on.

One day Brian noticed a strange telnet process running on a computer he 
was logged into.  He telnetted to the same port and discovered the Unix CB.
He got ahold of the code and with Craig Kanarick's help turned it into
vrave which has done more to bring far-flug ravers together than anyone can
imagine.

Articles in magazines, without knowing it, make passing references to
Brian's achievements with great frequency.  In the recent Rolling Stone
(with Anthony K. from the Red Hot Chili Peppers on the cover) there is
an article about techno and raving.  It starts out with a description of
a Full Moon Massive at Bonny Doon beach, a site which Brian first brought
to the attention of the raving community by throwing "Connection" down
there and then suggesting the site to Wicked for a Full Moon Party.  The
same article also noted that "talk about techno and raving on the 
Internet runs high," which is due in part to Brian's inspiration that
prompted the formation of all the raving mailing lists.

If that wasn't enough Brian set up the ftp/gopher/www site at for
raving at techno.stanford.edu, and the experienced he gained from that
got him a job managing the ftp/gopher/www site for Wired Magazine.  He's
gotten many positive compliments for his work on both sites, and is
helping to set the standard for good and interesting web sites in the
on-line publishing world.

Happy Birthday to Brian!!!

We love him!!!

Laura

Phred says:

>And this is the time to start
>thinking about *my* favorite idea, which is an all-weekend-long net.affair
>outside somewhere with 36+ hours of music and a relaxing good time for all.
>See you in . . . the future!

Yay!   I can hardly wait...  It's a long time since I was able to really
GET DOWN and boogie an entire weekend.    I hope I can get my car fixed soon
so I can start traveling around,  scouting for sites.

Say!  I got this killer idea,    Lets get together a small group of people
some weekend,  and go out driving around,   looking for suitable sites
to have killer outdoor gigs.   We could make a picnic/camping trip out
of it,   discover neat areas seldom visited by people.   Sorta like the
"Bay Area Backroads" places.     I remember a long time ago,  when I was
tinkering with the phone system,   I would go to some of the strangest
remotest places and hack their phone system.    All it takes is a good
map of California and the intention of having a good time exploring new
and strange places.     While I was visiting these places,  I would hang
out in the local gathering spots (pool halls,  etc),  and get to know the
locals.    That way, I was able to learn a lot about what goes on locally,
and I think that once we put forth the idea of having a rave/party in
their area,  they (The locals) would be more than willing to help us
get in contact with some of their friends who might have lots of private
land to have such a gig.    Most of the time,  at least in the summer,
these local folks living in remote areas would be really open to the idea
of having a real rave in their area.    It's worth checking out...

On the way up to Harbin Hot springs last summer,   I discovered an old 
race track out somewhere between San Rafael and Vallejo area (The Hiway
connecting the who cities),   and it appears to be far enough away from
homes.    I'll try and remember exactly where it is.   It was just as big,
if not bigger than the Livermore race track area where the Gathering was
held near the 4th of July (Remember the hill fire?).

Anyone else,  who goes driving around N. Calif should also keep a keen eye
out for such sites.    I think that it might be possible to locate the owners
of these places and negotiate a deal with them.   Of course we want the party
to be big enough to be fun,  but not super mega-large as to cause problems
in clean-up,  or other problems.    But predicting the size of such partys
is next to impossible.

Cap'n Crunch

Well I wasn't going to post until I got back from Seattle but the conferences
here today are boring so I might as well hang out in the terminal room :)

I was _very_ dissappointed in this FMM all around (maybe because I know a
little too much :) but let's just say that it could have been phenominal
with a little more planning.  Basically the sound sucked big time, this was 
due to the fact that the support poles for the high cabinets were forgotten
and thus the cabs could not be elevated abouve the crowd.  The sound system 
was also the perfect size for 300 people but not for 3000 (which is what my 
estimate of the crowd size is).  At 0300 Saturday I counted 1100 cars in the
2 miles on either side of bonnie doon.  I didn't drive up bonnie dune road
but I know from previous experience that you can easily park another 500
cars up there.  I know that Wicked was informed that this would be the largest
FMM ever.  The location chosen to set up the turntables was right under
the far clifs, THIS WAS VERY DANGEROUS! A dislodged rock (from the sonic
vibrations) could have easily killed a sleeping or dancing raver.
There were hords of drunk and tweeking people and I was offered speed more
than once during the night.

I suppose it did get better when Markie came on, I managed to get closer to
the sound system and Markie did deliver the goods.  Seeing all the familiar
faces and lots of smiles made me feel a little better but seeing all of the
trash on the beach (especially the spent baloons from nitrous consumption)
didn't make me feel happy. (I remember when the beach was _always_ left
spotless, I hate to think of what state it was left in this time)
So I must say that I didn't get to hear Jeno's set. I had to leave at 0830
in order to get on a plane to Seattle.  I hope Jeno did manage to pull it
out in the 11th hour, In my opinion the party really needed it.

To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU

Even though its getting late in the week, i would like to share my own 
feelings on the FMR.  Lee and i made some really excellent time getting to 
bonny doone beach (1:15 minutes) and upon arrival saw as many cars in one 
place as we've ever seen -- it was a mega event.  I knew that it was going 
to be great when we parked and happenned to run into friends parking 
next to us -- which was really weird considering how many people were 
there.  Much to my delight and surprise the weather at 4:00 a.m. was 
remarkably warm and comfortable. The sound at first was not good and wasn't 
helped by all the people parked in front of the speakers, but by 6:00 or 
7:00 a.m. the crowd was much thinned and Markie was out of this world.  He 
played for hours and let us hear some new things, most remarkable.  Jeno's 
set was almost scary it was so great, and the people dancing seemed 
possessed by some kind of rave spirit.  

The crowd was strange...it took a while for the unity to come together, but 
when it did it was awsome; by around 10:00 most of the clueless were gone 
and what was left was one of the most beautiful scenes of togetherness.  I 
can't see why there have been so many negative posts about the party by 
people who left way  before it was over.  However, I do blame part of the
problem on the fact that there was quite a bit of alcohol there.  I must
sadly admit that a lot of these people left their garbage behind (i.e., 
beer bottles and snack wrappers) much more so than any FMR party i've ever 
been to.  I regret to say that Lee and I forgot our garbage bags and didn't 
clean up as much as we would have liked to or usually do.  

All in all, i would say that this party was a reaffirmation in my faith 
that the scene is not dead.  There was plenty of good feeling and postive 
energy.  Lately there has been much complaining about the "scene" being 
on its way out; perhaps its just a matter of getting out of things what you 
put into it.  Keep the energy up and the postive vibe alive and things will 
go on...

janie

This Frdiay night, April 1st, a group from Paramount is
sponsoring a party at the Trocadero to be filmed for an 
interactive CD-ROM.  As I understand the CD is in three
parts: I forget the first, the second is a trip through
GG Park w/Rollerblading etc., and the third is a rave.
There will be scripted scenes with actors taking place
before the doors open: a smart bar scene and a chill
room scene are that I know about for sure.

The bulk of the footage will be spontaneous-- live shots of
people dancing, etc.  It sounds kinda neat to me.  Who
knows if they'll be "true" to what really goes down, but

people with some experience call the shots.  (Sean, one

To: "San FranDisco Ravers List" <sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU>
Subject: Re: FMM 
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Wed, 30 Mar 94 16:07:26 PST."
             <9403310007.AA08056@pbssi.srv.PacBell.COM> 
Date: Wed, 30 Mar 94 20:14:14 -0800
From: "Niels P. Mayer" <mayer@netcom.com>
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

From: lxfogel@srv.pacbell.com (Lee Fogel)
> This was very sad.  I would say that most of the mess was made by those
> who came and left early.  And that mess is highly representative of the
> kind of mentality (alchohol, nitrous, "let's just hang out for a few 
> hours") that is the antithesis of a good rave vibe.  For me, these parties
> don't really start until that element is reduced.  Too bad you had to 
> leave when things were just starting to really take off.

Well, there's two issues here. (1) mess, (2) coming and leaving early. 
A better question to ask is -- why not start earlier? I haven't
bothered w/ a FMR laterly because they start so FFing late that it
really  throws me for a loop.  W/r/t (1), perhaps if the parties
weren't so temporally skewed, people might have the time and energy to
show the caring that we've grown to expect from ravers. Insead, because
it's so marginalized and difficult to attend, you get attendees that do
nothing more than a quick wham-bam-thank-you-m'am party.

> There's a lesson to be learned here:  Take a nap, show up late.

Except for the times when the party moves. And then you end up driving
1.5 hrs for nothing; or finding out after the fact that it got
relocated to  candlestick (10 minutes away from home). And I have
yet to find out about relocated FMRs until after the fact, since
that info is only disseminated to those that stuck it out all night.

I remember some damn fine FMRs up at the Cummings Skyway Exit near
Pinole which started early (midnight) and ended in the morning.... In
that day (he says while smoking a corncob pipe and rocking in a creaky
chair) FMR sites were left pretty damn clean.

Also, it really is quite unsafe to plan a party where you've forced
most of your attendees to stay up all night, then party all day,  then
drive home for 1-2hrs. They'll either be driving while  extremely
tired; or driving while tired and coming down from whatever it took to
get them to stay up all night. I need not mention some of the serious
FMR-related driving injuries that have happened in the past, ostensibly
for such reasons.

--------------------

I have have long been sick of the "FMR is for serious ravers/insiders
only" attitude  that follows from the planning of FMRs. Basically, if
you've got  nothing else going on in your life or your life==raving,
then you can hack it. Otherwise if you've got personal
projects/interests, work, family, etc then you're *out* because you're
just not going to be able to waste all that time/effort/sleep looking
for a party. Doesn't sound very all-inclusive to me.

I'm sure someone's going to counter with "so you want your raves handed
to you on a silver platter"; It's not that at all -- but I don't think
i should have to shove a spool of barbed-wire through my ear,
sledgehammer it through my brain, and then pull it through the other
side (all while smiling gleefully!) just to rave. (I hate it when that
happens!)

I, for one, am looking forward to one-off outdoor parties, e.g.  MESS,
New Moon Rave, LiquidAir/SoundVision, Connection, etc...

   -- Niels "could be sour grapes cuz I was out of town too!" Mayer.

Why I Like Dance Music.

Because a gangsta from Long Beach bites Michael McDonald's rhythms and calls it G-Funk.

Because a curly haired white boy from Marin samples Isaac Hayes and Fat Albert along with Bono and Bruce Springsteen, calling it Transcendental Funk.

Because two lads from England use Perry Como in a thick fucking jam.

Because you hear it when you're eating unagi maki in a yuppie college town.

Because you hear it when you're eating pizza on the street downtown.

Because it liberates the mind.

Because it liberates the ass.

Why I Like Dance Music.

trance@netcom.com

  Southbound: Past University Avenue 

* Left at the first signal - W. Bayshore
  (it's a frontage road that takes you south again)

* Follow this road approx. 1/4 mile (pass apartment complexes on right)
  
* You will see the park on your right hand side. Turn into the first 
  driveway on your right.

* We'll meet on the grassy knoll , behind the round baseball fence.
  Next to the restrooms and ball courts.

Bring lunch, toys, yourselves!

    WILL NOT pay $0.25 for that big glass of water!

2.  you can't pass an empty warehouse, church, school, big open field, barn,
    airplane hanger, phone booth, nuclear power plant, etc...without getting

    a ...'

1.  and even then you're not a TRUE RAVER...because no one but myself
    can possibly THINK about calling themselves a TRUE RAVER!

	Suppose there was a net-service provider in the Bay Area which
charged only $10-$15/month.

	Suppose also that this provider was dedicated to keeping the
dialin linesavailable such that you would rarely get a busy signal.
	Suppose that this service was not run by an impersonal
provider but someone who was active in the sfraves communtiy, who was
very interested in helping the net-raver community through the service
that s/he will be providing.
	Also suppose that the person running the service was strongly
dedicated to personal privacy & anonymity, active in the cypherpunks
community.


	Suppose that the person running the service would like to help
out on sfraves parties which are internet connected.

	Now, given two negative points.. that at the outset: 1) The
net connection to the service would only be a 14.4 link. [I.e. it will
be a realtime link, but trying to telnet in/out would be tortuous and
file transfers will be slow] 2) The only dialups will be in
Berkeley/510.
	(These negative points would only be at the outset.. but..)

	Would you sign up?

I'm trying to see if this is feasible.


Please reply privately. Thanks.

-Sameer

At larger parties, perhaps offering a reward would give people an
incentive to clean up. If the mess gets to be major, pass around trash
bags, and give people who bring in a bag of trash a $4 off coupon to
the next Wicked, or perhaps a laminate, or whatever low-cost item
would be enough do it. (I'd do it for a bagel & tea :)).

This worked famously at Womad, where they gave away one free Ben &
Jerry's coupon to each person who brought in a bag of trash. When the
100,000 people cleared out from the all-day event, the place was
fairly clean. Nothing that a cleanup crew couldn't deal with in a
short amount of time.  A construction site sized dumpster near the
front was piled 20 feet high with kitchen size garbage bags people had
turned in.

Well it's just an idea. I'm kinda bummed too that people won't clean
up after themselves. If I think of anything else I'll post it.

Sean

(I've been to a few computer shows, and you'd be surprised what stupid
gyrations a $100,000 a year corporate executive will go through to
earn a trinket worth 30 cents.)

ought to have three months' worth of enthusiasm going for it...
(it's also got some competition tonight, but I encourage you to go
to both, if you're thinking of going to Spring Bash).  

Saturday night is a combined Basics and Come/Unity, which is supposed
to be outdoors, and I think the weather's supposed to be nice. (!)

thanks for all of the updates I've been getting via e-mail, and
keep 'em coming!

I had to go to the post office for my area of San Francisco
the other day, and outside of it they had LARGE stacks of
wooden pallets, the kind of things they use in warehouses
for the fork lifts to pick up.  

There was a sign on the wall next to the pallets saying "free
wood."

So, if you feel so inclined, they might make some good bonfire
fuel.  It's not recyling, but it is reusing which is also a
Good Thing to do.

To get the this particular post office head East on Army Street.
When you get to 3rd Street turn right.  Go over the little
drawbridge and make your second left onto Burke.  The post office
is the huge warehouse on the left.

Laura
